deserter want of provision for a supply of which they have not take the requisite precaution the hope spring from the venetic war and -lrb- also -rrb- because in most case man willingly believe what grant rejoice as if victory be fully certain they collect faggot and brushwood with which to fill up the roman trench and hasten to the camp xix -- the situation of the camp be a rise ground gently battle that they could not stand one attack of we man and immediately turn they back : and we man with full vigor follow they while disorder and slew a great number of they the horse pursue the rest leave but few who escape by flight thus at the same time sabinus be inform of the naval battle and caesar of victory gain by sabinus and all the state immediately surrender themselves to titurius : for as the temper of the gaul be impetuous and ready to undertake war so they mind be weak and by no means resolute in enduring calamity xx -- about the same time p crassus when he have arrive in another part adcantuannus who hold the chief command with 600 devoted follower whom they call soldurius -lrb- the condition of whose association be these -- that they enjoy all the convenience of life with those to whose friendship they have devote themselves : if anything calamitous happen to they either they endure the same destiny together with they or commit suicide : nor hitherto in the memory of man have there be find any one who upon he be slay to whose friendship he have devote himself refuse to die -rrb- adcantuannus -lrb- i say -rrb- endeavor to make a sally with these when we soldier have rush together to arm upon a shout be raise at that part of the fortification and a fierce battle have be fight there be drive back into the town yet he obtain from crassus -lrb- the indulgence -rrb- that he should enjoy the same term of surrender -lrb- as the other inhabitant -rrb- xxiii -- crassus have receive they arm and hostage march into the territory of the vocate and the tarusate but then the barbarian be alarm because they have hear that a town fortify by the nature of the place and by art have be take by we in a few day after we arrival there begin to send ambassador into all quarter to combine to give hostage one to another to raise troops ambassador also be send to those state of hither spain which be nearest to aquitanium and auxiliary and leader be summon from they on whose arrival they proceed to carry on the war with great confidence and with a great host of man they who have be with q sertorius the whole period -lrb- of he war in spain -rrb- and be suppose to have very great skill in military matter be choose leader these adopt the practice of the roman people begin to select -lrb- advantageous -rrb- place to fortify they camp to cut off we man from provision which when crassus observe -lrb- and likewise -rrb- that he force on account of they small number could not safely be separate that the enemy both make excursion and beset the pass and -lrb- yet -rrb- leave sufficient guard for they camp that on that account corn and provision could not very conveniently be bring up to he and that the number of the enemy be daily increase he think that he ought not to delay in give battle this matter be bring to a council when he discover that all think the same thing he appoint the next day for the fight xxiv -- have draw out all he force at the break of day and marshal they in a double line he post the auxiliary in the center and wait to see what measure the enemy would take they although on account of they great number and they ancient renown in war and the small number of we man they suppose they might safely fight nevertheless consider it safer to gain the victory without any wound by beset the pass -lrb- and -rrb- cut off the provision : and if the roman on account of the want of corn should begin to retreat they intend to attack they while encumber in they march and depress in spirit -lrb- as be assail while -rrb- under baggage this measure be approve of by the leader and the force of the roman draw out the enemy -lrb- still -rrb- keep themselves in they camp crassus have remark this circumstance since the enemy intimidate by they own delay and by the reputation -lrb- _ ie _ for cowardice arise thence -rrb- have render we soldier more eager for fight and the remark of all be hear -lrb- declare -rrb- that no longer ought delay to be make in go to the camp after encourage he man he march to the camp of the enemy to the great gratification of he own troops xxv -- there while some be fill up the ditch and other by throw a large number of dart be drive the defender from the rampart and fortification and the auxiliary on whom crassus do not much rely in the battle by supply stone and weapon -lrb- to the soldier -rrb- and by convey turf to the mound present the appearance and character of man engage in fight while also the enemy be fight resolutely and boldly and they weapon discharge from they higher position fall with great effect the horse have go round the camp of the enemy report to crassus that the camp be not fortify with equal care on the side of the decuman gate and have a easy approach xxvi -- crassus have exhort the commander of the horse to animate they man by great reward and promise point out to they what he wish to have do they as they have be command have bring out the four cohort which as they have be leave as a guard for the camp be not fatigue by exertion and have lead they round by a somewhat longer way lest they could be see from the camp of the enemy when the eye and mind of all be intent upon the battle quickly arrive at those fortification which we have speak of and have demolish these stand in the camp of the enemy before they be see by they or it be know what be go on and then a shout be hear in that quarter we man they strength have be recruit -lrb- which usually occur on the hope of victory -rrb- begin to fight more vigorously the enemy surround on all side -lrb- and -rrb- all they affair be despair of make great attempt to cast themselves down over the rampart and to seek safety in flight these the cavalry pursue over the very open plain and after leave scarcely a fourth part out of the number of 50000 which it be certain have assemble out of aquitanium and from the cantabrus return late at night to the camp xxvii -- have hear of this battle the greatest part of aquitanium surrender itself to crassus and of its own accord send hostage in which number be the tarbellus the bigerrione the precianus the vocasate the tarusate the elurate the garite the auscus the garumnus the sibuzate the cocosate a few -lrb- and those -rrb- most remote nation rely on the time of the year because winter be at hand neglect to do this xxviii -- about the same time caesar although the summer be nearly past yet since all gaul be reduce the morinus and the menapius alone remain in arm and have never send ambassador to he -lrb- to make a treaty -rrb- of peace speedily lead he army thither think that that war might soon be terminate they resolve to conduct the war on a very different method from the rest of the gaul for as they perceive that the greatest nation -lrb- of gaul -rrb- who have engage in war have be route and overcome and as they possess continuous range of forest and morass they remove themselves and all they property thither when caesar have arrive at the opening of these forest and have begin to fortify he camp and no enemy be in the meantime see while we man be disperse on they respective duty they suddenly rush out from all part of the forest and make a attack on we man the latter quickly take up arm and drive they back again to they forest and have kill a great many lose a few of they own man while pursue they too far through those intricate place xxix -- during the remain day after this caesar begin to cut down the forest and that no attack might be make on the flank of the soldier while unarmed and not foresee it he place together -lrb- opposite to the enemy -rrb- all that timber which be cut down and pile it up as a rampart on either flank when a great space have be with incredible speed clear in a few day when the cattle -lrb- of the enemy -rrb- and the rear of they baggage-train be already seize by we man and they themselves be seek for the thickest part of the forest storm of such a kind come on that the work be necessarily suspend and through the continuance of the rain the soldier could not any longer remain in they tent therefore have lay waste all they country -lrb- and -rrb- have burn they village and house caesar lead back he army and station they in winter-quarter among the aulercus and lexovius and the other state which have make war upon he last book iv i-the follow winter -lrb- this be the year in which cn pompey and m crassus be consul -rrb- those german -lrb- call -rrb- the usipete and likewise the tenchtherus with a great number of man cross the rhine not far from the place at which that river discharge itself into the sea the motive for cross -lrb- that river -rrb- be that have be for several year harass by the suevus they be constantly engage in war and hinder from the pursuit of agriculture the nation of the suevus be by far the largest and the most warlike nation of all the german they be say to possess a hundred canton from each of which they yearly send from they territory for the purpose of war a thousand armed man : the other who remain at home maintain -lrb- both -rrb- themselves and those engage in the expedition the latter again in they turn be in arm the year after : the former remain at home thus neither husbandry nor the art and practice of war be neglect but among they there exist no private and separate land nor be they permit to remain more than one year in one place for the purpose of residence they do not live much on corn but subsist for the most part on milk and flesh and be much -lrb- engage -rrb- in hunting which circumstance must by the nature of they food and by they daily exercise and the freedom of they life -lrb- for have from boyhood be accustom to no employment or discipline they do nothing at all contrary to they inclination -rrb- both promote they strength and render they man of vast stature of body and to such a habit have they bring themselves that even in the coldest part they wear no clothing whatever except skin by reason of the scantiness of which a great portion of they body be bare and besides they bathe in open river ii -- merchant have access to they rather that they may have person to whom they may sell those thing which they have take in war than because they need any commodity to be import to they moreover even as to labor cattle in which the gaul take the greatest pleasure and which they procure at a great price the german do not employ such as be import but those poor and ill-shaped animal which belong to they country these however they render capable of the greatest labor by daily exercise in cavalry action they frequently leap from they horse and fight on foot and train they horse to stand still in the very spot on which they leave they to which they retreat with great activity when there be occasion nor accord to they practice be anything regard as more unseemly or more unmanly than to use housing accordingly they have the courage though they be themselves but few to advance against any number whatever of horse mount with housing they on no account permit wine to be import to they because they consider that man degenerate in they power of endure fatigue and be render effeminate by that commodity iii -- they esteem it they greatest praise as a nation that the land about they territory lie unoccupied to a very great extent inasmuch as -lrb- they think -rrb- that by this circumstance be indicate that a great number of nation can not withstand they power and thus on one side of the suevus the land be say to lie desolate for about six hundred mile on the other side they border on the ubius whose state be large and flourishing consider the condition of the german and who be somewhat more refined than those of the same race and the rest -lrb- of the german -rrb- and that because they border on the rhine and be much resort to by merchant and be accustom to the manners of the gaul by reason of they approximity to they though the suevus after make the attempt frequently and in several war could not expel this nation from they territory on account of the extent and population of they state yet they make they tributary and render they less distinguished and powerful -lrb- than they have ever be -rrb- iv -- in the same condition be the usipete and the tenchtherus -lrb- whom we have mention above -rrb- who for many year resist the power of the suevus but be at last drive from they possession and have wander through many part of germany come to the rhine to district which the menapius inhabit and where they have land house and village on either side of the river the latter people alarm by the arrival of so great a multitude remove from those house which they have on the other side of the river and have place guard on this side the rhine proceed to hinder the german from cross they find themselves after they have try all means unable either to force a passage on account of they deficiency in shipping or cross by stealth on account of the guard of the menapius pretend to return to they own settlement and district and after have proceed three day ' march return and they cavalry have perform the whole of this journey in one night cut off the menapius who be ignorant of and do not expect -lrb- they approach and -rrb- who have moreover be inform of the departure of the german by they scout have without apprehension return to they village beyond the rhine have slay these and seize they ship they cross the river before that part of the menapius who be at peace in they settlement over the rhine be apprise of -lrb- they intention -rrb- and seize all they house maintain themselves upon they provision during the rest of the winter v -- caesar when inform of these matter fear the fickle disposition of the gaul who be easily prompt to take up resolution and much addict to change consider that nothing be to be entrust to they for it be the custom of that people to compel traveller to stop even against they inclination and inquire what they may have hear or may know respect any matter and in town the common people throng around merchant and force they to state from what country they come and what affair they know of there they often engage in resolution concern the most important matter induce by these report and story alone of which they must necessarily instantly repent since they yield to mere unauthorised report and since most people give to they question answer frame agreeably to they wish vi -- caesar be aware of they custom in order that he might not encounter a more formidable war set forward to the army earlier in the year than he be accustom to do when he have arrive there he discover that those thing which he have suspect would occur have take place that embassy have be send to the german by some of the state and that they have be entreat to leave the rhine and have be promise that all thing which they desire should be provide by the gaul allure by this hope the german be then make excursion to greater distance and have advance to the territory of the eburone and the condrusus who be under the protection of the trevirus after summon the chief of gaul caesar think proper to pretend ignorance of the thing which he have discover and have conciliate and confirm they mind and order some cavalry to be raise resolve to make war against the german vii -- have provide corn and select he cavalry he begin to direct he march towards those part in which he hear the german be when he be distant from they only a few day ' march ambassador come to he from they state whose speech be as follow : -- that the german neither make war upon the roman people first nor do they decline if they be provoke to engage with they in arm for that this be the custom of the german hand down to they from they forefather to resist whatsoever people make war upon they and not to avert it by entreaty this however they confess -- that they have come hither reluctantly have be expel from they country if the roman be dispose to accept they friendship they might be serviceable ally to they and let they either assign they land or permit they to retain those which they have acquire by they arm that they be inferior to the suevus alone to whom not even the immortal god can show themselves equal that there be none at all besides on earth whom they could not conquer viii -- to these remark caesar reply in such term as he think proper but the conclusion of he speech be that he could make no alliance with they if they continue in gaul that it be not probable that they who be not able to defend they own territory should get possession of those of other nor be there any land lie waste in gaul which could be give away especially to so great a number of man without do wrong -lrb- to other -rrb- but they might if they be desirous settle in the territory of the ubius whose ambassador be then with he and be complain of the aggression of the suevus and request assistance from he and that he would obtain this request from they ix -- the ambassador say that they would report these thing to they countryman and after have deliberate on the matter would return to caesar after the third day they beg that he would not in the meantime advance he camp nearer to they caesar say that he could not grant they even that for he have learn that they have send a great part of they cavalry over the meuse to the ambivaritus some day before for the purpose of plunder and procure forage he suppose that they be then wait for these horse and that the delay be cause on this account x -- the meuse rise from mount le vosge which be in the territory of the lingone and have receive a branch of the rhine which be call the waal form the island of the batavus and not more than eighty mile from it it fall into the ocean but the rhine take its course among the lepontius who inhabit the alp and be carry with a rapid current for a long distance through the territory of the sarunate helvetii sequani mediomatricus tribucus and trevirus and when it approach the ocean divide into several branch and have form many and extensive island a great part of which be inhabit by savage and barbarous nation -lrb- of whom there be some who be suppose to live on fish and the egg of sea-fowl -rrb- flow into the ocean by several mouth xi -- when caesar be not more than twelve mile distant from the enemy the ambassador return to he as have be arrange who meet he on the march earnestly entreat he not to advance any farther when they could not obtain this they beg he to send on a despatch to those who have march in advance of the main army and forbid they to engage and grant they permission to send ambassador to the ubius and if the prince and senate of the latter would give they security by oath they assure caesar that they would accept such condition as might be propose by he and request that he would give they the space of three day for negotiate these affair caesar think that these thing tend to the self-same point -lrb- as they other proposal -rrb- -lrb- namely -rrb- that in consequence of a delay of three day intervene they horse which be at a distance might return however he say that he would not that day advance farther than four mile for the purpose of procure water he order that they should assemble at that place in as large a number as possible the follow day that he might inquire into they demand in the meantime he send messenger to the officer who have march in advance with all the cavalry to order they not to provoke the enemy to a engagement and if they themselves be assail to sustain the attack until he come up with the army xii -- but the enemy as soon as they see we horse the number of which be 5000 whereas they themselves have not more than 800 horse because those which have go over the meuse for the purpose of forage have not return while we man have no apprehension because they ambassador have go away from caesar a little before and that day have be request by they as a period of truce make a onset on we man and soon throw they into disorder when we man in they turn make a stand they accord to they practice leap from they horse to they foot and stab we horse in the belly and overthrow a great many of we man put the rest to flight and drive they forward so much alarm that they do not desist from they retreat till they have come in sight of we army in that encounter seventy-four of we horse be slay among they piso a aquitanian a most valiant man and descend from a very illustrious family whose grandfather have hold the sovereignty of he state and have be style friend by we senate he while he be endeavor to render assistance to he brother who be surround by the enemy and whom he rescue from danger be himself throw from he horse which be wound under he but still oppose -lrb- he antagonist -rrb- with the greatest intrepidity as long as he be able to maintain the conflict when at length he fall surround on all side and after receive many wound and he brother who have then retire from the fight observe it from a distance he spur on he horse throw himself upon the enemy and be kill xiii -- after this engagement caesar consider that neither ought ambassador to be receive to audience nor condition be accept by he from those who after have sue for peace by way of stratagem and treachery have make war without provocation and to wait till the enemy 's force be augmented and they cavalry have return he conclude would be the greatest madness and know the fickleness of the gaul he feel how much influence the enemy have already acquire among they by this one skirmish he -lrb- therefore -rrb- deem that no time for convert measure ought to be afford they after have resolve on these thing and communicate he plan to he lieutenant and quaestor in order that he might not suffer any opportunity for engage to escape he a very seasonable event occur namely that on the morning of the next day a large body of german consist of they prince and old man come to the camp to he to practice the same treachery and dissimulation but as they assert for the purpose of acquit themselves for have engage in a skirmish the day before contrary to what have be agree and to what indeed they themselves have request and also if they could by any means obtain a truce by deceive he caesar rejoice that they have fall into he power order they to be detain he then draw all he force out of the camp and command the cavalry because he think they be intimidate by the late skirmish to follow in the rear xiv -- have marshal he army in three line and in a short time perform a march of eight mile he arrive at the camp of the enemy before the german could perceive what be go on who be suddenly alarm by all the circumstance both by the speediness of we arrival and the absence of they own officer as time be afford neither for concert measure nor for seize they arm be perplex as to whether it would be better to lead out they force against the enemy or to defend they camp or seek they safety by flight they consternation be make apparent by they noise and tumult we soldier excite by the treachery of the precede day rush into the camp : such of they as could readily get they arm for a short time withstand we man and give battle among they cart and baggage-waggon but the rest of the people -lrb- consist -rrb- of boy and woman -lrb- for they have leave they country and cross the rhine with all they family -rrb- begin to fly in all direction in pursuit of whom caesar send the cavalry xv -- the german when upon hear a noise behind they -lrb- they look and -rrb- see that they family be be slay throw away they arm and abandon they standard flee out of the camp and when they have arrive at the confluence of the meuse and the rhine the survivor despair of farther escape as a great number of they countryman have be kill throw themselves into the river and there perish overcome by fear fatigue and the violence of the stream we soldier after the alarm of so great a war for the number of the enemy amount to 430000 return to they camp all safe to a man very few be even wound caesar grant those whom he have detain in the camp liberty of depart they however dread revenge and torture from the gaul whose land they have harass say that they desire to remain with he caesar grant they permission xvi -- the german war be finish caesar think it expedient for he to cross the rhine for many reason of which this be the most weighty that since he see the german be so easily urge to go into gaul he desire they should have they fear for they own territory when they discover that the army of the roman people both could and dare pass the rhine there be add also that that portion of the cavalry of the usipete and the tenchtherus which i have above related to have cross the meuse for the purpose of plunder and procure forage and be not present at the engagement have betake themselves after the retreat of they countryman across the rhine into the territory of the sigambrus and unite themselves to they when caesar send ambassador to they to demand that they should give up to he those who have make war against he and against gaul they reply that the rhine bound the empire of the roman people if he do not think it just for the german to pass over into gaul against he consent why do he claim that anything beyond the rhine should be subject to he dominion or power the ubius also who alone out of all the nation lie beyond the rhine have send ambassador to caesar and form a alliance and give hostage earnestly entreat that he would bring they assistance because they be grievously oppress by the suevus or if he be prevent from do so by the business of the commonwealth he would at least transport he army over the rhine that that would be sufficient for they present assistance and they hope for the future that so great be the name and the reputation of he army even among the most remote nation of the german arise from the defeat of ariovistus and this last battle which be fight that they might be safe under the fame and friendship of the roman people they promise a large number of ship for transport the army xvii -- caesar for those reason which i have mention have resolve to cross the rhine but to cross by ship he neither deem to be sufficiently safe nor considered consistent with he own dignity or that of the roman people therefore although the greatest difficulty in form a bridge be present to he on account of the breadth rapidity and depth of the river he nevertheless consider that it ought to be attempt by he or that he army ought not otherwise to be lead over he devise this plan of a bridge he join together at the distance of two foot two pile each a foot and a half thick sharpen a little at the lower end and proportion in length to the depth of the river after he have by means of engine sink these into the river and fix they at the bottom and then drive they in with rammer not quite perpendicularly like a stake but bend forward and slope so as to incline in the direction of the current of the river he also place two -lrb- other pile -rrb- opposite to these at the distance of forty foot lower down fasten together in the same manner but direct against the force and current of the river both these moreover be keep firmly apart by beam two foot thick -lrb- the space which the binding of the pile occupy -rrb- lay in at they extremity between two brace on each side and in consequence of these be in different direction and fasten on side the one opposite to the other so great be the strength of the work and such the arrangement of the material that in proportion as the greater body of water dash against the bridge so much the closer be its part hold fasten together these beam be bind together by timber lay over they in the direction of the length of the bridge and be -lrb- then -rrb- cover over with lath and hurdle and in addition to this pile be drive into the water obliquely at the lower side of the bridge and these serve as buttress and be connect with every portion of the work sustain the force of the stream : and there be other also above the bridge at a moderate distance that if trunk of tree or vessel be float down the river by the barbarian for the purpose of destroy the work the violence of such thing might be diminish by these defence and might not injure the bridge xviii -- within ten day after the timber begin to be collect the whole work be complete and the whole army lead over caesar leave a strong guard at each end of the bridge hasten into the territory of the sigambrus in the meantime ambassador from several nation come to he whom on they sue for peace and alliance he answer in a courteous manner and order hostage to be bring to he but the sigambrus at the very time the bridge be begin to be build make preparation for a flight -lrb- by the advice of such of the tenchtherus and usipete as they have amongst they -rrb- and quit they territory and convey away all they possession and conceal themselves in desert and wood xix -- caesar have remain in they territory a few day and burnt all they village and house and cut down they corn proceed into the territory of the ubius and have promise they he assistance if they be ever harass by the suevus he learn from they these particulars : that the suevus after they have by means of they scout find that the bridge be be build have call a council accord to they custom and send order to all part of they state to remove from the town and convey they child wife and all they possession into the wood and that all who could bear arm should assemble in one place that the place thus choose be nearly the center of those region which the suevus possess that in this spot they have resolve to await the arrival of the roman and give they battle there when caesar discover this have already accomplish all those thing on account of which he have resolve to lead he army over namely to strike fear into the german take vengeance on the sigambrus and free the ubius from the invasion of the suevus have spend altogether eighteen day beyond the rhine and think he have advance far enough to serve both honor and interest he return into gaul and cut down the bridge xx -- during the short part of summer which remain caesar although in these country as all gaul lie towards the north the winter be early nevertheless resolve to proceed into britain because he discover that in almost all the war with the gaul succor have be furnish to we enemy from that country and even if the time of year should be insufficient for carry on the war yet he think it would be of great service to he if he only enter the island and see into the character of the people and get knowledge of they locality harbor and landing-place all which be for the most part unknown to the gaul for neither do any one except merchant generally go thither nor even to they be any portion of it known except the sea-coast and those part which be opposite to gaul therefore after have call up to he the merchant from all part he could learn neither what be the size of the island nor what or how numerous be the nation which inhabit it nor what system of war they follow nor what custom they use nor what harbor be convenient for a great number of large ship xxi -- he send before he caius volusenus with a ship of war to acquire a knowledge of these particulars before he in person should make a descent into the island as he be convince that this be a judicious measure he commission he to thoroughly examine into all matter and then return to he as soon as possible he himself proceed to the morinus with all he force he order ship from all part of the neighbouring country and the fleet which the precede summer he have build for the war with the venetus to assemble in this place in the meantime he purpose have be discover and report to the briton by merchant ambassador come to he from several state of the island to promise that they will give hostage and submit to the government of the roman people have give they a audience he after promise liberally and exhort they to continue in that purpose send they back to they own country and -lrb- despatch -rrb- with they commius whom upon subdue the atrebate he have create king there a man whose courage and conduct he esteem and who he think would be faithful to he and whose influence rank highly in those country he order he to visit as many state as he could and persuade they to embrace the protection of the roman people and apprise they that he would shortly come thither volusenus have view the locality as far as means could be afford one who dare not leave he ship and trust himself to barbarian return to caesar on the fifth day and report what he have there observe xxii -- while caesar remain in these part for the purpose of procure ship ambassador come to he from a great portion of the morinus to plead they excuse respect they conduct on the late occasion allege that it be as man uncivilised and as those who be unacquainted with we custom that they have make war upon the roman people and promise to perform what he should command caesar think that this have happen fortunately enough for he because he neither wish to leave a enemy behind he nor have a opportunity for carry on a war by reason of the time of year nor consider that employment in such trifling matter be to be prefer to he enterprise on britain impose a large number of hostage and when these be bring he receive they to he protection have collect together and provide about eighty transport ship as many as he think necessary for convey over two legion he assign such -lrb- ship -rrb- of war as he have besides to the quaestor he lieutenant and officer of cavalry there be in addition to these eighteen ship of burden which be prevent eight mile from that place by wind from be able to reach the same port these he distribute amongst the horse the rest of the army he deliver to q titurius sabinus and l aurunculeius cotta he lieutenant to lead into the territory of the menapius and those canton of the morinus from which ambassador have not come to he he order p sulpicius rufus he lieutenant to hold possession of the harbor with such a garrison as he think sufficient xxiii -- these matter be arrange find the weather favourable for he voyage he set sail about the third watch and order the horse to march forward to the farther port and there embark and follow he as this be perform rather tardily by they he himself reach britain with the first squadron of ship about the fourth hour of the day and there see the force of the enemy draw up in arm on all the hill the nature of the place be this : the sea be confine by mountain so close to it that a dart could be throw from they summit upon the shore consider this by no mean a fit place for disembark he remain at anchor till the ninth hour for the other ship to arrive there have in the meantime assemble the lieutenant and military tribune he tell they both what he have learn from volusenus and what he wish to be do and enjoin they -lrb- as the principle of military matter and especially as maritime affair which have a precipitate and uncertain action require -rrb- that all thing should be perform by they at a nod and at the instant have dismiss they meet both with wind and tide favourable at the same time the signal be give and the anchor weigh he advance about seven mile from that place and station he fleet over against a open and level shore xxiv -- but the barbarian upon perceive the design of the roman send forward they cavalry and charioteer a class of warrior of whom it be they practice to make great use in they battle and follow with the rest of they force endeavor to prevent we man landing in this be the greatest difficulty for the follow reason namely because we ship on account of they great size could be station only in deep water and we soldier in place unknown to they with they hand embarrassed oppress with a large and heavy weight of armor have at the same time to leap from the ship stand amidst the wave and encounter the enemy whereas they either on dry ground or advance a little way into the water free in all they limb in place thoroughly know to they could confidently throw they weapon and spur on they horse which be accustom to this kind of service dismayed by these circumstance and altogether untrained in this mode of battle we man do not all exert the same vigor and eagerness which they have be wont to exert in engagement on dry ground xxv -- when caesar observe this he order the ship of war the appearance of which be somewhat strange to the barbarian and the motion more ready for service to be withdraw a little from the transport vessel and to be propel by they oar and be station towards the open flank of the enemy and the enemy to be beat off and drive away with sling arrow and engine : which plan be of great service to we man for the barbarian be startle by the form of we ship and the motion of we oar and the nature of we engine which be strange to they stop and shortly after retreat a little and while we man be hesitate -lrb- whether they should advance to the shore -rrb- chiefly on account of the depth of the sea he who carry the eagle of the tenth legion after supplicate the god that the matter might turn out favourably to the legion exclaim leap fellow soldier unless you wish to betray you eagle to the enemy i for my part will perform my duty to the commonwealth and my general when he have say this with a loud voice he leap from the ship and proceed to bear the eagle toward the enemy then we man exhort one another that so great a disgrace should not be incur all leap from the ship when those in the nearest vessel see they they speedily follow and approach the enemy xxvi -- the battle be maintain vigorously on both side we man however as they could neither keep they rank nor get firm footing nor follow they standard and as one from one ship and another from another assemble around whatever standard they meet be throw into great confusion but the enemy who be acquaint with all the shallows when from the shore they see any come from a ship one by one spur on they horse and attack they while embarrassed many surround a few other throw they weapon upon we collect force on they expose flank when caesar observe this he order the boat of the ship of war and the spy sloop to be fill with soldier and send they up to the succor of those whom he have observe in distress we man as soon as they make good they footing on dry ground and all they comrade have join they make a attack upon the enemy and put they to flight but could not pursue they very far because the horse have not be able to maintain they course at sea and reach the island this alone be want to caesar 's accustomed success xxvii -- the enemy be thus vanquish in battle as soon as they recover after they flight instantly send ambassador to caesar to negotiate about peace they promise to give hostage and perform what he should command together with these ambassador come commius the atrebatian who as i have above say have be send by caesar into britain he they have seize upon when leave he ship although in the character of ambassador he bear the general 's commission to they and throw into chain : then after the battle be fight they send he back and in sue for peace cast the blame of that act upon the common people and entreat that it might be pardon on account of they indiscretion caesar complain that after they have sue for peace and have voluntarily send ambassador into the continent for that purpose they have make war without a reason say that he would pardon they indiscretion and impose hostage a part of whom they give immediately the rest they say they would give in a few day since they be send for from remote place in the meantime they order they people to return to the country part and the chief assemble from all quarter and proceed to surrender themselves and they state to caesar xxviii -- a peace be establish by these proceedings four day after we have come into britain the eighteen ship to which reference have be make above and which convey the cavalry set sail from the upper port with a gentle gale when however they be approach britain and be see from the camp so great a storm suddenly arise that none of they could maintain they course at sea and some be take back to the same port from which they have start -- other to they great danger be drive to the lower part of the island nearer to the west which however after have cast anchor as they be get fill with water put out to sea through necessity in a stormy night and make for the continent xxix -- it happen that night to be full moon which usually occasion very high tide in that ocean and that circumstance be unknown to we man thus at the same time the tide begin to fill the ship of war which caesar have provide to convey over he army and which he have draw up on the strand and the storm begin to dash the ship of burden which be ride at anchor against each other nor be any means afford we man of either manage they or of render any service a great many ship have be wreck inasmuch as the rest have lose they cable anchor and other tackle be unfit for sail a great confusion as would necessarily happen arise throughout the army for there be no other ship in which they could be convey back and all thing which be of service in repair vessel be want and corn for the winter have not be provide in those place because it be understand by all that they would certainly winter in gaul xxx -- on discover these thing the chief of britain who have come up after the battle be fight to perform those condition which caesar have impose hold a conference when they perceive that cavalry and ship and corn be want to the roman and discover the small number of we soldier from the small extent of the camp -lrb- which too be on this account more limited than ordinary because caesar have convey over he legion without baggage -rrb- and think that the best plan be to renew the war and cut off we man from corn and provision and protract the affair till winter because they feel confident that if they be vanquish or cut off from a return no one would afterwards pass over into britain for the purpose of make war therefore again enter into a conspiracy they begin to depart from the camp by degree and secretly bring up they people from the country part xxxi -- but caesar although he have not as yet discover they measure yet both from what have occur to he ship and from the circumstance that they have neglect to give the promise hostage suspect that the thing would come to pass which really do happen he therefore provide remedy against all contingency for he daily convey corn from the country part into the camp use the timber and brass of such ship as be most seriously damage for repair the rest and order whatever thing besides be necessary for this object to be bring to he from the continent and thus since that business be execute by the soldier with the greatest energy he effect that after the loss of twelve ship a voyage could be make well enough in the rest xxxii -- while these thing be be transact one legion have be send to forage accord to custom and no suspicion of war have arise as yet and some of the people remain in the country part other go backwards and forwards to the camp they who be on duty at the gate of the camp report to caesar that a greater dust than be usual be see in that direction in which the legion have march caesar suspect that which be -lrb- really the case -rrb- -- that some new enterprise be undertake by the barbarian order the two cohort which be on duty to march into that quarter with he and two other cohort to relieve they on duty the rest to be arm and follow he immediately when he have advance some little way from the camp he see that he man be overpower by the enemy and scarcely able to stand they ground and that the legion be crowd together weapon be be cast on they from all side for as all the corn be reap in every part with the exception of one the enemy suspect that we man would repair to that have conceal themselves in the wood during the night then attack they suddenly scatter as they be and when they have lay aside they arm and be engage in reap they kill a small number throw the rest into confusion and surround they with they cavalry and chariot xxxiii -- they mode of fight with they chariot be this : firstly they drive about in all direction and throw they weapon and generally break the rank of the enemy with the very dread of they horse and the noise of they wheel and when they have work themselves in between the troops of horse leap from they chariot and engage on foot the charioteer in the meantime withdraw some little distance from the battle and so place themselves with the chariot that if they master be overpower by the number of the enemy they may have a ready retreat to they own troops thus they display in battle the speed of horse -lrb- together with -rrb- the firmness of infantry and by daily practice and exercise attain to such expertness that they be accustom even on a decline and steep place to check they horse at full speed and manage and turn they in a instant and run along the pole and stand on the yoke and thence betake themselves with the greatest celerity to they chariot again xxxiv-under these circumstance we man be dismay by the novelty of this mode of battle caesar most seasonably bring assistance for upon he arrival the enemy pause and we man recover from they fear upon which think the time unfavourable for provoke the enemy and come to a action he keep himself in he own quarter and a short time have intervene draw back the legion into the camp while these thing be go on and all we man engage the rest of the briton who be in the field depart storm then set in for several successive day which both confine we man to camp and hinder the enemy from attack we in the meantime the barbarian despatch messenger to all part and report to they people the small number of we soldier and how good a opportunity be give for obtain spoil and for liberating themselves for ever if they should only drive the roman from they camp have by these means speedily get together a large force of infantry and of cavalry they come up to the camp xxxv -- although caesar anticipate that the same thing which have happen on former occasion would then occur -- that if the enemy be route they would escape from danger by they speed still have get about thirty horse which commius the atrebatian of whom mention have be make have bring over with he -lrb- from gaul -rrb- he draw up the legion in order of battle before the camp when the action commence the enemy be unable to sustain the attack of we man long and turn they back we man pursue they as far as they speed and strength permit and slew a great number of they then have destroy and burnt everything far and wide they retreat to they camp xxxvi -- the same day ambassador send by the enemy come to caesar to negotiate a peace caesar double the number of hostage which he have before demand and order that they should be bring over to the continent because since the time of the equinox be near he do not consider that with he ship out of repair the voyage ought to be defer till winter have meet with favourable weather he set sail a little after midnight and all he fleet arrive safe at the continent except two of the ship of burden which could not make the same port which the other ship do and be carry a little lower down xxxvii -- when we soldier about 300 in number have be draw out of these two ship and be march to the camp the morinus whom caesar when set forth for britain have leave in a state of peace excite by the hope of spoil at first surround they with a small number of man and order they to lay down they arm if they do not wish to be slay afterwards however when they form a circle stand on they defense a shout be raise and about 6000 of the enemy soon assemble which be report caesar send all the cavalry in the camp as a relief to he man in the meantime we soldier sustain the attack of the enemy and fight most valiantly for more than four hour and receive but few wound themselves slew several of they but after we cavalry come in sight the enemy throw away they arm turn they back and a great number of they be kill xxxviii -- the day follow caesar send labienus he lieutenant with those legion which he have bring back from britain against the morinus who have revolt who as they have no place to which they might retreat on account of the dry up of they marsh -lrb- which they have avail themselves of as a place of refuge the precede year -rrb- almost all fall into the power of labienus in the meantime caesar 's lieutenant q titurius and l cotta who have lead the legion into the territory of the menapius have lay waste all they land cut down they corn and burn they house return to caesar because the menapius have all conceal themselves in they thickest wood caesar fix the winter quarter of all the legion amongst the belgae thither only two british state send hostage the rest omit to do so for these success a thanksgiving of twenty day be decree by the senate upon receive caesar 's letter book v i -- lucius domitius and appius claudius be consul caesar when depart from he winter quarter into italy as he have be accustom to do yearly command the lieutenant whom he appoint over the legion to take care that during the winter as many ship as possible should be build and the old repair he plan the size and shape of they for despatch of lading and for draw they on shore he make they a little lower than those which we have be accustom to use in we sea and that into hither gaul and proceed thence to the army when he have arrive there have make a survey of the winter quarter he find that by the extraordinary ardor of the soldier amidst the utmost scarcity of with four legion without baggage and 800 horse because they neither come to the general diet -lrb- of gaul -rrb- nor obey he command and be moreover say to be tamper with the german beyond the rhine iii -- this state be by far the most powerful of all gaul in cavalry and have great force of infantry and as we have remark above border on the rhine in that state two person indutiomarus and cingetorix be then contend with each other for the supreme power one of whom as soon as the arrival of caesar and he legion be know come to he assure he that he and all he party would continue in they allegiance and not revolt from the alliance of the roman people and inform he of the thing which be go on amongst the trevirus but indutiomarus begin to collect cavalry and infantry and make preparation for war have conceal those who by reason of they age could not be under arm in the forest arduenna which be of immense size -lrb- and -rrb- extend from the rhine across the country of the trevirus to the frontier of the remus but after that some of the chief person of the state both influence by they friendship for cingetorix and alarm at the arrival of we army come to caesar and begin to solicit he privately about they own interest since they could not provide for the safety of the state indutiomarus dread lest he should be abandon by all send ambassador to caesar to declare that he absent himself from he countryman and refrain from come to he on this account that he might the more easily keep the state in its allegiance lest on the departure of all the nobility the commonalty should in they indiscretion revolt and thus the whole state be at he control and that he if caesar would permit would come to the camp to he and would commit he own fortune and those of the state to he good faith iv -- caesar though he discern from what motive these thing be say and what circumstance deter he from he meditated plan still in order that he might not be compel to waste the summer among the trevirus while all thing be prepare for the war with britain order indutiomarus to come to he with 200 hostage when these be bring -lrb- and -rrb- among they he son and near relation whom he have demand by name he console indutiomarus and enjoin he to continue in he allegiance yet nevertheless summon to he the chief man of the trevirus he reconcile they individually to cingetorix : this which have be build in the country of the meldus have be drive back by a storm have be unable to maintain they course and have return to the same port from which they have set out he find the rest together with the other dumnorix the aeduan of whom we have make previous mention he in particular he have resolve to have with he because he have discover he to be fond of change fond of power which speech the aeduus bear with impatience and yet dare not send ambassador to caesar for the purpose of either reject or deprecate -lrb- that appointment -rrb- that fact caesar have learn from he all those whom he fear to slay in the sight of gaul to pledge he honor to the rest to ask for they oath that they would by common deliberation execute what they should perceive to be necessary for -rrb- nevertheless learn all he measure : have at length meet with favourable weather he order the foot soldier and the horse to embark in the ship but while the mind of all be occupy dumnorix begin exclaim that he be free and the subject of a free state they surround and kill the man as they have be command but the aeduan horseman all return to caesar viii -- when these thing be do -lrb- and -rrb- labienus leave on the continent with three legion and 2000 horse to defend the harbor and provide corn and discover what be go on in gaul and take measure accord to the occasion and accord to the circumstance he himself with five legion and a number of horse equal to that which he be leave on the continent set sail at sunset and -lrb- though for a time -rrb- bear forward by a gentle soldier be very much to be extol for they with the transport and heavy ship the labor of rowing not be -lrb- for a moment -rrb- discontinue equal the speed of the ship of war all the ship reach the enemy have lodge themselves have leave ten cohort and 300 horse at the sea to be a guard to the ship hasten to the enemy at the third watch fear the less for the ship for this reason because he be leave they fasten at anchor upon a even and open shore and he place q atrius over the guard of the ship he himself have advance by night about twelve mile espy the force of the enemy they advance to the river with they cavalry and chariot from the higher ground begin to annoy we man and give battle be repulse by we cavalry they conceal themselves in wood as they have secure a place admirably fortify by nature and by art which as it seem they have before prepare on account of a civil war for all entrance to it be shut up by a great number of fell tree they themselves rush out of the wood great part of the day be spend he wish time to be leave for the fortification of the camp x -- the next day early in the morning he send both foot-soldier and horse in three division on a expedition a very great storm have arise almost all the ship be dash to piece and cast upon the shore because neither the anchor and cable could resist nor could the sailor and pilot sustain the violence of the the chief command and management of the war have be entrust to cassivellaunus whose territory a river which be call the thame separate from the maritime state at about eighty mile from the sea at a earlier period perpetual war have take place between he and the other state but greatly alarm by we arrival the briton have place he over the whole war and the conduct of it xii -- the interior portion of britain be inhabit by those of whom they say that it be hand down by tradition that they be bear in the island itself : the maritime portion by those who have pass over from the country of the belgae for the purpose of plunder and make war almost all of whom be call by the name of those state from which be spring they go thither and have wage war continue there and begin to cultivate the land the number of the people be countless and they building exceedingly numerous for the most part very like those of the gaul : the number of cattle be great they use either brass or iron ring determine at a certain weight as they money tin be produce in the midland region in the maritime iron but the quantity of it be small : they employ brass which be import there as in gaul be timber of every description except beech and fir they do not regard it lawful to eat the hare and the cock and the goose they however breed they for amusement and pleasure the climate be more temperate than in gaul the cold be less severe xiii -- the island be triangular in its form and one of its side be opposite to gaul one angle of this side which be in kent whither almost all ship from gaul be direct -lrb- look -rrb- to the east the lower look to the south this side extend about 500 mile another side lie towards spain and the west on which part be ireland less as be reckon than britain by one-half but the passage -lrb- from it -rrb- into britain be of equal distance with that from gaul in the middle of this voyage be a island which be call mona many smaller island besides be suppose to lie -lrb- there -rrb- of which island some have write that at the time of the winter solstice it be night there for thirty consecutive day we in we inquiry about that matter ascertain nothing except that by accurate measurement with water we perceive the night to be shorter there than on the continent the length of this side as they account state be 700 mile the third side be towards the north to which portion of the island no land be opposite but a angle of that side look principally towards germany this side be consider to be 800 mile in length thus the whole island be -lrb- about -rrb- 2000 mile in circumference xiv -- the most civilised of all these nation be they who inhabit kent which be entirely a maritime district nor do they differ much from the gallic custom most of the inland inhabitant do not sow corn but live on milk and flesh and be clothe with skin all the briton indeed dye themselves with wood which occasion a bluish color and thereby have a more terrible appearance in fight they wear they hair long and have every part of they body shave except they head and upper lip ten and even twelve have wife common to they and particularly brother among brother and parent among they child but if there be any issue by these wife they be repute to be the child of those by whom respectively each be first espouse when a virgin xv -- the horse and charioteer of the enemy contend vigorously in a skirmish with we cavalry on the march yet so that we man be conqueror in all part and drive they to they wood and hill but have slay a great many they pursue too eagerly and lose some of they man but the enemy after some time have elapse when we man be off they guard and occupy in the fortification of the camp rush out of the wood and make a attack upon those who be place on duty before the camp fight in a determine manner and two cohort be send by caesar to they relief and these severally the first of two legion when these have take up they position at a very small distance from each other as we man be disconcert by the unusual mode of battle the enemy break through the middle of they most courageously and retreat thence in safety that day q laberius durus a tribune of the soldier be slay the enemy since more cohort be send against they be repulse xvi -- in the whole of this method of fight since the engagement take place under the eye of all and before the camp it be perceive that we man on account of the weight of they arm inasmuch as they could neither pursue -lrb- the enemy when -rrb- retreat nor dare quit they standard be little suit to this kind of enemy that the horse also fight with great danger because they -lrb- the briton -rrb- generally retreat even designedly and when they have draw off we man a short distance from the legion leap from they chariot and fight on foot in unequal -lrb- and to they advantageous -rrb- battle but the system of cavalry engagement be wont to produce equal danger and indeed the same both to those who retreat and those who pursue to this be add that they never fight in close order but in small party and at great distance and have detachment place -lrb- in different part -rrb- and then the one relieve the other and the vigorous and fresh succeed the wearied xvii -- the follow day the enemy halt on the hill a distance from we camp and present themselves in small party and begin to challenge we horse to battle with less spirit than the day before but at noon when caesar have send three legion and all the cavalry with c trebonius the lieutenant for the purpose of forage they fly upon the until the horse rely on relief as they see the legion behind they drive the enemy precipitately before they and slaying a great number of they do not give they the opportunity either of rally or halt or leap from they chariot immediately after this retreat the auxiliary who have assemble from all side depart nor after that time do the enemy ever engage with we in very large number xviii -- caesar discover they design lead he army into the territory of cassivellaunus to the river thame which river can be ford in one place only and that with difficulty when he have arrive there he perceive that numerous force of the enemy be marshal on the other bank of the river the bank also be defend by sharp stake fix in front and stake of the same kind fix under the water be cover by the river these thing be discover from -lrb- some -rrb- prisoner and deserter caesar send forward the cavalry order the legion to follow they immediately but the soldier advance with such speed and such ardor though have state above all hope -lrb- rise out -rrb- of battle be lay aside the greater part of he force be dismiss and about 4000 charioteer only be leave use to observe we march and retire a little from the road and conceal himself in intricate and woody place and in those neighborhood in which he have discover we be about to march he use to drive the cattle and the inhabitant from the field into the wood and when we cavalry for the sake of plunder and ravage the more freely scatter themselves among the field he use to send out charioteer from the wood by all the well-known road and path and to the great danger of we horse engage with they and this source of fear hinder they from straggle very extensively the result be that caesar do not allow excursion to be make to a great distance from the main body of the legion and order that damage should be do to the enemy in ravage they land and kindle fire only so far as the legionary soldier could by they own exertion and march accomplish it xx -- in the meantime the trinobante almost the most powerful state of those part from which the young man mandubratius embrace the protection of caesar have come to the continent of gaul to -lrb- meet -rrb- he -lrb- whose father imanuentius have possess the sovereignty in that state and have be kill by cassivellaunus he himself have escape death by flight -rrb- send ambassador to caesar and the corn xxi -- the trinobante be protect and secure from any violence of the soldier the cenimagnus the segontiacus the ancalite the bibrocus and the cassus send embassy surrender themselves to caesar from they he learn that the capital town of cassivellaunus be not far from that place and be defend by wood and morass and a very large number of man and of cattle have be collect in it -lrb- now the briton when they have fortify the intricate wood in which they be wont to assemble for the purpose of avoid the incursion of a enemy with a entrenchment and a rampart call they a town -rrb- thither he proceed with he legion : he find the place admirably fortify by nature and art he however undertake to attack it in two direction the enemy have remain only a short time do not sustain the
