reader a account of the manners of gaul and germany and wherein these nation differ from each other in gaul there be faction not only in all the state and in all the canton and they division but almost in each family and of these faction those be the leader who be consider accord to they judgment to possess the greatest influence upon whose will and determination the management of all affair and measure depend and that seem to have be institute in ancient time with this view that no one of the common people should be in want of support against one more powerful for none -lrb- of those leader -rrb- suffer he party to be oppress and defraud and if he do otherwise he have no influence among he party this same policy exist throughout the whole of gaul for all the state be divide into two faction xii -- when caesar arrive in gaul the aeduus be the leader of one faction the sequanus of the other since the latter be less powerful by themselves inasmuch as the chief influence be from of old among the aeduus and they dependency be great they have unite to themselves the german and ariovistus and have bring they over to they party by great sacrifice and promise and have fight several successful battle and slay all the nobility of the aeduus they have so far surpass they in power that they bring over from the aeduus to themselves a large portion of they dependant and receive from they the son of they lead man as hostage and compel they to swear in they public character that they would enter into no design against they and hold a portion of the neighbouring land seize on by force and possess the sovereignty of the whole of gaul divitiacus urge by this necessity have proceed to rome to the senate for the purpose of entreat assistance and have return without accomplish he object a change of affair ensue on the arrival of caesar the hostage be return to the aeduus they old dependency restore and new acquire through caesar -lrb- because those who have attach themselves to they alliance see that they enjoy a better state and a milder government -rrb- they other interest they influence they reputation be likewise increase and in consequence the sequanus lose the sovereignty the remus succeed to they place and as it be perceive that they equal the aeduus in favor with caesar those who on account of they old animosity could by no means coalesce with the aeduus consign themselves in clientship to the remus the latter carefully protect they thus they possess both a new and suddenly acquire influence affair be then in that position that the aeduus be consider by far the lead people and the remus hold the second post of honor xiii -- throughout all gaul there be two order of those man who be of any rank and dignity : for the commonality be hold almost in the condition of slave and dare to undertake nothing of itself and be admit to no deliberation the greater part when they be press either by debt or the large amount of they tribute or the oppression of the more powerful give themselves up in vassalage to the noble who possess over they the same rights without exception as master over they slave but of these two order one be that of the druid the other that of the knight the former be engage in thing sacred conduct the public and the private sacrifice and interpret all matter of religion to these a large number of the young man resort for the purpose of instruction and they -lrb- the druid -rrb- be in great honor among they for they determine respect almost all controversy public and private and if any crime have be perpetrate if murder have be commit if there be any dispute about a inheritance if any about boundary these same person decide it they decree reward and punishment if any one either in a private or public capacity have not submit to they decision they interdict he from the sacrifice this among they be the most heavy punishment those who have be thus interdict be esteem in the number of the impious and the criminal : all shun they and avoid they society and conversation lest they receive some evil from they contact nor be justice administer to they when seek it nor be any dignity bestow on they over all these druid one preside who possess supreme authority among they upon he death if any individual among the rest be pre-eminent in dignity he succeed but if there be many equal the election be make by the suffrage of the druid sometimes they even contend for the presidency with arm these assemble at a fixed period of the year in a consecrate place in the territory of the carnute which be reckon the central region of the whole of gaul hither all who have dispute assemble from every part and submit to they decree and determination this institution be suppose to have be devise in britain and to have be bring over from it into gaul and now those who desire to gain a more accurate knowledge of that system generally proceed thither for the purpose of study it xiv -- the druid do not go to war nor pay tribute together with the rest they have a exemption from military service and a dispensation in all matter induce by such great advantage many embrace this profession of they own accord and -lrb- many -rrb- be send to it by they parent and relation they be say there to learn by heart a great number of verse accordingly some remain in the course of training twenty year nor do they regard it lawful to commit these to write though in almost all other matter in they public and private transaction they use greek character that practice they seem to I to have adopt for two reason because they neither desire they doctrine to be divulge among the mass of the people nor those who learn to devote themselves the less to the effort of memory rely on write since it generally occur to most man that in they dependence on write they relax they diligence in learn thoroughly and they employment of the memory they wish to inculcate this as one of they lead tenet that soul do not become extinct but pass after death from one body to another and they think that man by this tenet be in a great degree excite to valor the fear of death be disregard they likewise discuss and impart to the youth many thing respect the star and they motion respect the extent of the world and of we earth respect the nature of thing respect the power and the majesty of the immortal god xv -- the other order be that of the knight these when there be occasion and any war occur -lrb- which before caesar 's arrival be for the most part wont to happen every year as either they on they part be inflict injury or repel those which other inflict on they -rrb- be all engage in war and those of they most distinguish by birth and resource have the greatest number of vassal and dependant about they they acknowledge this sort of influence and power only xvi -- the nation of all the gaul be extremely devote to superstitious rite and on that account they who be trouble with unusually severe disease and they who be engage in battle and danger either sacrifice man as victim or vow that they will sacrifice they and employ the druid as the performer of those sacrifice because they think that unless the life of a man be offer for the life of a man the mind of the immortal god can not be render propitious and they have sacrifice of that kind ordain for national purpose other have figure of vast size the limb of which form of osier they fill with live man which be set on fire the man perish envelop in the flame they consider that the oblation of such as have be take in theft or in robbery or any other offence be more acceptable to the immortal god but when a supply of that class be want they have recourse to the oblation of even the innocent xvii -- they worship as they divinity mercury in particular and have many image of he and regard he as the inventor of all art they consider he the guide of they journey and march and believe he to have very great influence over the acquisition of gain and mercantile transaction next to he they worship apollo and mar and jupiter and minerva respect these deity they have for the most part the same belief as other nation : that apollo avert disease that minerva impart the invention of manufacture that jupiter possess the sovereignty of the heavenly power that mar preside over war to he when they have determine to engage in battle they commonly vow those thing they shall take in war when they have conquer they sacrifice whatever capture animal may have survive the conflict and collect the other thing into one place in many state you may see pile of these thing heap up in they consecrate spot nor do it often happen that any one disregard the sanctity of the case dare either to secrete in he house thing capture or take away those deposit and the most severe punishment with torture have be establish for such a deed xviii -- all the gaul assert that they be descend from the god di and say that this tradition have be hand down by the druid for that reason they compute the division of every season not by the number of day but of night they keep birthday and the beginning of month and year in such a order that the day follow the night among the other usage of they life they differ in this from almost all other nation that they do not permit they child to approach they openly until they be grow up so as to be able to bear the service of war and they regard it as indecorous for a son of boyish age to stand in public in the presence of he father xix -- whatever sum of money the husband have receive in the name of dowry from they wife make a estimate of it they add the same amount out of they own estate a account be keep of all this money conjointly and the profit be lay by : whichever of they shall have survive -lrb- the other -rrb- to that one the portion of both revert together with the profit of the previous time husband have power of life and death over they wife as well as over they child : and when the father of a family bear in a more than commonly distinguish rank have die he relation assemble and if the circumstance of he death be suspicious hold a investigation upon the wife in the manner adopt towards slave and if proof be obtain put they to severe torture and kill they they funeral consider the state of civilization among the gaul be magnificent and costly and they cast into the fire all thing include live creature which they suppose to have be dear to they when alive and a little before this period slave and dependant who be ascertain to have be beloved by they be after the regular funeral rite be complete burn together with they xx -- those state which be consider to conduct they commonwealth more judiciously have it ordain by they law that if any person shall have hear by rumor and report from he neighbor anything concern the commonwealth he shall convey it to the magistrate and not impart it to any other because it have be discover that inconsiderate and inexperienced man be often alarm by false report and drive to some rash act or else take hasty measure in affair of the highest importance the magistrate conceal those thing which require to be keep unknown and they disclose to the people whatever they determine to be expedient it be not lawful to speak of the commonwealth except in council xxi -- the german differ much from these usage for they have neither druid to preside over sacred office nor do they pay great regard to sacrifice they rank in the number of the god those alone whom they behold and by whose instrumentality they be obviously benefit namely the sun fire and the moon they have not hear of the other deity even by report they whole life be occupy in hunting and in the pursuit of the military art from childhood they devote themselves to fatigue and hardship those who have remain chaste for the longest time receive the greatest commendation among they people : they think that by this the growth be promote by this the physical power be increase and the sinew be strengthened and to have have knowledge of a woman before the twentieth year they reckon among the most disgraceful act of which matter there be no concealment because they bathe promiscuously in the river and -lrb- only -rrb- use skin or small cloak of deer ' hide a large portion of the body be in consequence naked xxii -- they do not pay much attention to agriculture and a large portion of they food consist in milk cheese and flesh nor have any one a fix quantity of land or he own individual limit but the magistrate and the lead man each year apportion to the tribe and family who have unite together as much land as and in the place in which they think proper and the year after compel they to remove elsewhere for this enactment they advance many reason -- lest seduce by long-continued custom they may exchange they ardor in the wage of war for agriculture lest they may be anxious to acquire extensive estate and the more powerful drive the weaker from they possession lest they construct they house with too great a desire to avoid cold and heat lest the desire of wealth spring up from which cause division and discord arise and that they may keep the common people in a contented state of mind when each see he own means place on a equality with -lrb- those of -rrb- the most powerful xxiii -- it be the greatest glory to the several state to have as wide desert as possible around they they frontier have be lay waste they consider this the real evidence of they prowess that they neighbor shall be drive out of they land and abandon they and that no one dare settle near they at the same time they think that they shall be on that account the more secure because they have remove the apprehension of a sudden incursion when a state either repel war wage against it or wages it against another magistrate be choose to preside over that war with such authority that they have power of life and death in peace there be no common magistrate but the chief of province and canton administer justice and determine controversy among they own people robbery which be commit beyond the boundary of each state bear no infamy and they avow that these be commit for the purpose of discipline they youth and of prevent sloth and when any of they chief have say in a assembly that he will be they leader let those who be willing to follow give in they name they who approve of both the enterprise and the man arise and promise they assistance and be applaud by the people such of they as have not follow he be account in the number of deserter and traitor and confidence in all matter be afterwards refuse they to injure guest they regard as impious they defend from wrong those who have come to they for any purpose whatever and esteem they inviolable to they the house of all be open and maintenance be freely supply xxiv -- and there be formerly a time when the gaul excel the german in prowess and wage war on they offensively and on account of the great number of they people and the insufficiency of they land send colony over the rhine accordingly the volcae tectosage seize on those part of germany which be the most fruitful -lrb- and lie -rrb- around the hercynian forest -lrb- which i perceive be know by report to eratosthene and some other greek and which they call orcynium -rrb- and settle there which nation to this time retain its position in those settlement and have a very high character for justice and military merit : now also they continue in the same scarcity indigence hardihood as the german and use the same food and dress but they proximity to the province and knowledge of commodity from country beyond the sea supply to the gaul many thing tend to luxury as well as civilization accustom by degree to be overmatch and worst in many engagement they do not even compare themselves to the german in prowess xxv -- the breadth of this hercynian forest which have be refer to above be to a quick traveller a journey of nine day for it can not be otherwise compute nor be they acquaint with the measure of road it begin at the frontier of the helvetii nemete and rauracus and extend in a right line along the river danube to the territory of the dacus and the anarte : it bend thence to the leave in a different direction from the river and themselves to he when these affair be accomplish caesar march to the avaricum which be the largest and best fortify town in the territory of the biturige and situate in a most fertile tract of country noviodunum summons he man to a council he impress on they that the war must be prosecute on a very different system from that which have be previously adopt but they should by all mean aim at this object that the roman should be prevent from forage and procure provision that this be easy because they themselves be well supply with cavalry and be likewise assist by the season of the year that forage could not be cut that the enemy must necessarily disperse and look for it in the house that all these might be daily destroy by the horse besides that the interest of private property must be neglect for the sake of the general safety that the village and house ought to be fire over such a extent of country in every direction from boia as the roman appear capable of scour in they search for forage that a abundance of these necessaries could be supply to they because they would be assist by the resource of those in whose territory the war would be wage : that the roman either would not bear the privation or else would advance to any distance from the camp with considerable danger and that it make no difference whether they slew they or strip they of they baggage since if it be lose they could not carry on the war besides that the town ought to be burnt which be not secure against every danger by they fortification or natural advantage that there should not be place of retreat for they own countryman for decline military service nor be expose to the roman as inducement to carry off abundance of provision and plunder if these sacrifice should appear heavy or galling that they ought to consider it much more distressing that they wife and child should be drag off to slavery and themselves slay the evil which must necessarily befall the conquer xv -- this opinion have be approve of by unanimous consent more than twenty town of the biturige be burn in one day conflagration be behold in every quarter and although all bear this with great regret yet they lay before themselves this consolation that as the victory be certain they could quickly recover they loss there be a debate concern avaricum in the general council whether they should decide that it should be burnt or defend the biturige throw themselves at the foot of all the gaul and entreat that they should not be compel to set fire with they own hand to the fairest city of almost the whole of gaul which be both a protection and ornament to the state they say that they could easily defend it owe to the nature of the ground for be enclose almost on every side by a river and a marsh it have only one entrance and that very narrow permission be grant to they at they earnest request vercingetorix at first dissuade they from it but afterwards concede the point owe to they entreaty and the compassion of the soldier a proper garrison be select for the town xvi -- vercingetorix follow closely upon caesar by shorter march and select for he camp a place defend by wood and marsh at the distance of fifteen mile from avaricum there he receive intelligence by trusty scout every hour in the day of what be go on at avaricum and order whatever he wish to be do he closely watch all we expedition for corn and forage and whenever they be compel to go to a greater distance he attack they when disperse and inflict severe loss upon they although the evil be remedy by we man as far as precaution could be take by go forth at irregular time and by different way xvii -- caesar pitch he camp at that side of the town which be not defend by the river and marsh and have a very narrow approach as we have mention begin to raise the vinea and erect two tower for the nature of the place prevent he from draw a line of circumvallation he never cease to importune the boius and aeduus for supplies of corn of whom the one -lrb- the aeduus -rrb- because they be act with no zeal do not aid he much the other -lrb- the boius -rrb- as they resource be not great quickly consume what they have although the army be distressed by the greatest want of corn through the poverty of the boius the apathy of the aeduus and the burning of the house to such a degree that for several day the soldier be without corn and satisfy they extreme hunger with cattle drive from the remote village yet no language be hear from they unworthy of the majesty of the roman people and they former victory moreover when caesar address the legion one by one when at work and say that he would raise the siege if they feel the scarcity too severely they unanimously beg he not to do so that they have serve for several year under he command in such a manner that they never submit to insult and never abandon a enterprise without accomplish it that they should consider it a disgrace if they abandon the siege after commence it that it be better to endure every hardship than not to avenge the mane of the roman citizen who perish at genabum by the perfidy of the gaul they entrust the same declaration to the centurion and military tribune that through they they might be communicate to caesar xviii -- when the tower have now approach the wall caesar ascertain from the captive that vercingetorix after destroy the forage have pitch he camp nearer avaricum and that he himself with the cavalry and light-armed infantry who generally fight among the horse have go to lay a ambuscade in that quarter to which he think that we troops would come the next day to forage on learn these fact he set out from the camp secretly at midnight and reach the camp of the enemy early in the morning they have quickly learn the arrival of caesar by scout hide they car and baggage in the thickest part of the wood and draw up all they force in a lofty and open space : which circumstance be announce caesar immediately order the baggage to be pile and the arm to be get ready xix -- there be a hill of a gentle ascent from the bottom a dangerous and impassable marsh not more than fifty foot broad begirt it on almost every side the gaul have break down the bridge post themselves on this hill in confidence of they position and be draw up in tribe accord to they respective state hold all the ford and passage of that marsh with trusty guard thus determine that if the roman should attempt to force the marsh they would overpower they from the higher ground while stick in it so that whoever see the nearness of the position would imagine that the two army be prepare to fight on almost equal term but whoever should view accurately the disadvantage of position would discover that they be show off a empty affectation of courage caesar clearly point out to he soldier who be indignant that the enemy could bear the sight of they at the distance of so short a space and be earnestly demand the signal for action with how great loss and the death of how many gallant man the victory would necessarily be purchase : and when he see they so determine to decline no danger for he renown that he ought to be consider guilty of the utmost injustice if he do not hold they life dearer than he own personal safety have thus console he soldier he lead they back on the same day to the camp and determine to prepare the other thing which be necessary for the siege of the town xx -- vercingetorix when he have return to he man be accuse of treason in that he have move he camp nearer the roman in that he have go away with all the cavalry in that he have leave so great force without a commander in that on he departure the roman have come at such a favourable season and with such despatch that all these circumstance could not have happen accidentally or without design that he prefer hold the sovereignty of gaul by the grant of caesar to acquire it by they favor be accuse in such a manner he make the following reply to these charge : -- that he move he camp have be cause by want of forage and have be do even by they advice that he approach near the roman have be a measure dictate by the favourable nature of the ground which would defend he by its natural strength that the service of the cavalry could not have be requisite in marshy ground and be useful in that place to which they have go that he on he departure have give the supreme command to no one intentionally lest he should be induce by the eagerness of the multitude to hazard a engagement to which he perceive that all be incline owe to they want of energy because they be unable to endure fatigue any longer that if the roman in the meantime come up by chance they -lrb- the gaul -rrb- should feel grateful to fortune if invite by the information of some one they should feel grateful to he because they be enable to see distinctly from the higher ground the smallness of the number of they enemy and despise the courage of those who not daring to fight retreat disgracefully into they camp that he desire no power from caesar by treachery since he could have it by victory which be now assure to himself and to all the gaul nay that he would even give they back the command if they think that they confer honor on he rather then receive safety from he that you may be assure say he that i speak these word with truth -- listen to these roman soldier he produce some camp-follower whom he have surprise on a forage expedition some day before and have tortured by famine and confinement they be previously instruct in what answer they should make when examine say that they be legionary soldier that urge by famine and want they have recently go forth from the camp -lrb- to see -rrb- if they could find any corn or cattle in the field that the whole army be distressed by a similar scarcity nor have any one now sufficient strength nor could bear the labor of the work and therefore that the general be determine if he make no progress in the siege to draw off he army in three day these benefit say vercingetorix you receive from I whom you accuse of treason -- I by whose exertion you see so powerful and victorious a army almost destroy by famine without shed one drop of you blood and i have take precaution that no state shall admit within its territory this army in its ignominious flight from this place xxi -- the whole multitude raise a shout and clash they arm accord to they custom as they usually do in the case of he whose speech they approve -lrb- they exclaim -rrb- that vercingetorix be a consummate general and that they have no doubt of he honor that the war could not be conduct with greater prudence they determine that ten thousand man should be pick out of the entire army and send into the town and decide that the general safety should not be entrust to the biturige alone because they be aware that the glory of the victory must rest with the biturige if they make good the defense of the town xxii -- to the extraordinary valor of we soldier device of every sort be oppose by the gaul since they be a nation of consummate ingenuity and most skilful in imitate and make those thing which be impart by any one for they turn aside the hook with noose and when they have catch hold of they firmly draw they on by means of engine and undermine the mound the more skilfully on this account because there be in they territory extensive iron mine and consequently every description of mining operation be know and practice by they they have furnish moreover the whole wall on every side with turret and have cover they with skin besides in they frequent sally by day and night they attempt either to set fire to the mound or attack we soldier when engage in the work and moreover by splicing the upright timber of they own tower they equal the height of ours as fast as the mound have daily raise they and countermine we mine and impede the working of they by stake bent and sharpen at the end and boiling pitch and stone of very great weight and prevent they from approach the wall xxiii -- but this be usually the form of all the gallic wall straight beam connect lengthwise and two foot distant from each other at equal interval be place together on the ground these be mortise on the inside and cover with plenty of earth but the interval which we have mention be close up in front by large stone these be thus lay and cement together another row be add above in such a manner that the same interval may be observe and that the beam may not touch one another but equal space intervene each row of beam be keep firmly in its place by a row of stone in this manner the whole wall be consolidate until the regular height of the wall be complete this work with respect to appearance and variety be not unsightly owe to the alternate row of beam and stone which preserve they order in right line and besides it possess great advantage as regard utility and the defense of city for the stone protect it from fire and the wood from the batter ram since it -lrb- the wood -rrb- be mortise in the inside with row of beam generally forty foot each in length can neither be break through nor torn asunder xxiv -- the siege have be impede by so many disadvantage the soldier although they be retard during the whole time by the mud cold and constant shower yet by they incessant labor overcome all these obstacle and in twenty-five day raise a mound three hundred and thirty foot broad and eighty foot high when it almost touch the enemy 's wall and caesar accord to he usual custom keep watch at the work and encourage the soldier not to discontinue the work for a moment : a little before the third watch they discover that the mound be sink since the enemy have set it on fire by a mine and at the same time a shout be raise along the entire wall and a sally be make from two gate on each side of the turret some at a distance be cast torch and dry wood from the wall on the mound other be pour on it pitch and other material by which the flame might be excite so that a plan could hardly be form as to where they should first run to the defense or to what part aid should be bring however as two legion always keep guard before the camp by caesar 's order and several of they be at stated time at the work measure be promptly take that some should oppose the sally party other draw back the tower and make a cut in the rampart and moreover that the whole army should hasten from the camp to extinguish the flame xxv -- when the battle be go on in every direction the rest of the night be now spend and fresh hope of victory always arise before the enemy : the more so on this account because they see the covering of we tower burn away and perceive that we be expose could not easily go to give assistance and they themselves be always relieve the weary with fresh man and consider that all the safety of gaul rest on this crisis there happen in my own view a circumstance which have appear to be worthy of record we think it ought not to be omit a certain gaul before the gate of the town who be cast into the fire opposite the turret ball of tallow and fire which be pass along to he be pierce with a dart on the right side and fall dead one of those next he step over he as he lay and discharge the same office : when the second man be slay in the same manner by a wound from a cross-bow a third succeed he and a fourth succeed the third : nor be this post leave vacant by the besiege until the fire of the mound have be extinguish and the enemy repulse in every direction a end be put to the fight xxvi -- the gaul have try every expedient as nothing have succeed adopt the design of flee from the town the next day by the advice and order of vercingetorix they hope that by attempt it at the dead of night they would effect it without any great loss of man because the camp of vercingetorix be not far distant from the town and the extensive marsh which intervene be likely to retard the roman in the pursuit and they be now prepare to execute this by night when the matron suddenly run out into the street and weep cast themselves at the foot of they husband and request of they with every entreaty that they should not abandon themselves and they common child to the enemy for punishment because the weakness of they nature and physical power prevent they from take to flight when they see that they -lrb- as fear do not generally admit of mercy in extreme danger -rrb- persist in they resolution they begin to shout aloud and give intelligence of they flight to the roman the gaul be intimidate by fear of this lest the pass should be pre-occupied by the roman cavalry desist from they design xxvii -- the next day caesar the tower be advance and the work which he have determine to raise be arrange a violent storm arise think this no bad time for execute he design because he observe the guard arrange on the wall a little too negligently and therefore order he own man to engage in they work more remissly and point out what he wish to be do he draw up he soldier in a secret position within the vinea and exhort they to reap at least the harvest of victory proportionate to they exertion he propose a reward for those who should first scale the wall and give the signal to the soldier they suddenly fly out from all quarter and quickly fill the wall xxviii -- the enemy be alarm by the suddenness of the attack be dislodge from the wall and tower and draw up in form of a wedge in the market-place and the open street with this intention that if a attack should be make on any side they should fight with they line draw up to receive it when they see no one descend to the level ground and the enemy extend themselves along the entire wall in every direction fear lest every hope of flight should be cut off they cast away they arm and seek without stop the most remote part of the town a part be then slay by the infantry when they be crowd upon one another in the narrow passage of the gate and a part have get without the gate be cut to piece by the cavalry : nor be there one who be anxious for the plunder thus be excite by the massacre at genabum and the fatigue of the siege they spare neither those wear out with year woman or child finally out of all that number which amount to about forty thousand scarcely eight hundred who flee from the town when they hear the first alarm reach vercingetorix in safety : and he the night be now far spend receive they in silence after they flight -lrb- fear that any sedition should arise in the camp from they entrance in a body and the compassion of the soldier -rrb- so that have arrange he friend and the chief of the state at a distance on the road he take precaution that they should be separate and conduct to they fellow countryman to whatever part of the camp have be assign to each state from the begin xxix -- vercingetorix have convene a assembly on the follow day console and encourage he soldier in the follow word : -- that they should not be too much depress in spirit nor alarmed at they loss that the roman do not conquer by valor nor in the field but by a kind of art and skill in assault with which they themselves be unacquainted that whoever expect every event in the war to be favourable err that it never be he opinion that avaricum should be defend of the truth of which statement he have themselves as witness but that it be owe to the imprudence of the biturige and the too ready compliance of the rest that this loss be sustain that however he would soon compensate it by superior advantage for that he would by he exertion bring over those state which sever themselves from the rest of the gaul and would create a general unanimity throughout the whole of gaul the union of which not even the whole earth could withstand and that he have it already almost effect that in the meantime it be reasonable that he should prevail on they for the sake of the general safety to begin to fortify they camp in order that they might the more easily sustain the sudden attack of the enemy xxx -- this speech be not disagreeable to the gaul principally because he himself be not dishearten by receive so severe a loss and have not conceal himself nor shun the eye of the people : and he be believe to possess greater foresight and sounder judgment than the rest because when the affair be undecided he have at first be of opinion that avaricum should be burnt and afterwards that it should be abandon accordingly as ill success weaken the authority of other general so on the contrary he dignity increase daily although a loss be sustain : at the same time they begin to entertain hope on he assertion of unite the rest of the state to themselves and on this occasion for the first time the gaul begin to fortify they camp and be so alarmed that although they be man unaccustomed to toil yet they be of opinion that they ought to endure and suffer everything which should be impose upon they xxxi -- nor do vercingetorix use less effort than he have promise to gain over the other state and -lrb- in consequence -rrb- endeavor to entice they leader by gift and promise for this object he select fitting emissary by whose subtle plead or private friendship each of the noble could be most easily influence he take care that those who flee to he on the storm of avaricum should be provide with arm and clothes at the same time that he diminished force should be recruit he levy a fixed quota of soldier from each state and define the number and day before which he should wish they bring to the camp and order all the archer of whom there be a very great number in gaul to be collect and send to he by these mean the troops which be lose at avaricum be speedily replace in the meantime teutomarus the son of ollovicon the king of the nitiobrige whose father have receive the appellation of friend from we senate come to he with a great number of he own horse and those whom he have hire from aquitanium xxxii -- caesar after delay several day at avaricum and finding there the greatest plenty of corn and other provision refresh he army after they fatigue and privation the winter be almost end when he be invite by the favourable season of the year to prosecute the war and march against the enemy -lrb- and try -rrb- whether he could draw they from the marsh and wood or else press they by a blockade some nobleman of the aeduus come to he as ambassador to entreat that in a extreme emergency he should succor they state that they affair be in the utmost danger because whereas single magistrate have be usually appoint in ancient time and hold the power of king for a single year two person now exercise this office and each assert that he be appoint accord to they law that one of they be convictolitanis a powerful and illustrious youth the other cotus spring from a most ancient family and personally a man of very great influence and extensive connection he brother valetiacus have bear the same office during the last year : that the whole state be up in arm the senate divide the people divide that each of they have he own adherent and that if the animosity would be foment any longer the result would be that one part of the state would come to a collision with the other that it rest with he activity and influence to prevent it xxxiii -- although caesar consider it ruinous to leave the war and the enemy yet be well aware what great evil generally arise from internal dissension lest a state so powerful and so closely connect with the roman people which he himself have always foster and honor in every respect should have recourse to violence and arm and that the party which have less confidence in its own power should summon aid from vercingetorix he determine to anticipate this movement and because by the law of the aeduus it be not permit those who hold the supreme authority to leave the country he determine to go in person to the aeduus lest he should appear to infringe upon they government and law and summon all the senate and those between whom the dispute be to meet he at decetium when almost all the state have assemble there and he be inform that one brother have be declare magistrate by the other when only a few person be privately summon for the purpose at a different time and place from what he ought whereas the law not only forbid two belong to one family to be elect magistrate while each be alive but even deter they from be in the senate he compel cotus to resign he office he order convictolitani who have be elect by the priest accord to the usage of the state in the presence of the magistrate to hold the supreme authority xxxiv -- have pronounce this decree between -lrb- the contend party -rrb- he exhort the aeduus to bury in oblivion they dispute and dissension and lay aside all these thing devote themselves to the war and expect from he on the conquest of gaul those reward which they should have earn and send speedily to he all they cavalry and ten thousand infantry which he might place in different garrison to protect he convoy of provision and then divide he army into two part : he give labienus four legion to lead into the country of the senone and parisius and lead in person six into the country of the arvernus in the direction of the town of gergovium along the bank of the allier he give part of the cavalry to labienus and keep part to himself vercingetorix on learn this circumstance break down all the bridge over the river and begin to march on the other bank of the allier xxxv -- when each army be in sight of the other and be pitch they camp almost opposite that of the enemy scout be distribute in every quarter lest the roman should build a bridge and bring over they troops it be to caesar a matter attend with great difficulty lest he should be hinder from pass the river during the greater part of the summer as the allier can not generally be ford before the autumn therefore that this might not happen have pitch he camp in a woody place opposite to one of those bridge which vercingetorix have take care should be break down the next day he stop behind with two legion in a secret place : he send on the rest of the force as usual with all the baggage after have select some cohort that the number of the legion might appear to be complete have order these to advance as far as they could when now from the time of day he conjecture they have come to a encampment he begin to rebuild the bridge on the same pile the lower part of which remain entire have quickly finish the work and lead he legion across he select a fit place for a camp and recall the rest of he troops vercingetorix on ascertain this fact go before he by force march in order that he might not be compel to come to a action against he will xxxvi -- caesar in five day ' march go from that place to gergovium and after engage in a slight cavalry skirmish that day on view the situation of the city which be build on a very high mountain be very difficult of access he despair of take it by storm and determine to take no measure with regard to besiege it before he should secure a supply of provision but vercingetorix have pitch he camp on the mountain near the town place the force of each state separately and at small interval around himself and have occupy all the hill of that range as far as they command a view -lrb- of the roman encampment -rrb- he present a formidable appearance he order the ruler of the state whom he have select as he council of war to come to he daily at the dawn whether any measure seem to require deliberation or execution nor do he allow almost any day to pass without testing in a cavalry action the archer be intermix what spirit and valor there be in each of he own man there be a hill opposite the town at the very foot of that mountain strongly fortify and precipitous on every side -lrb- which if we man could gain they seem likely to exclude the enemy from a great share of they supply of water and from free foraging but this place be occupy by they with a weak garrison -rrb- : however caesar set out from the camp in the silence of night and dislodge the garrison before succor could come from the town he get possession of the place and post two legion there and draw from the greater camp to the less a double trench twelve foot broad so that the soldier could even singly pass secure from any sudden attack of the enemy xxxvii -- whilst these affair be go on at gergovium convictolitani the aeduan to whom we have observe the magistracy be adjudge by caesar be bribe by the arvernus hold a conference with certain young man the chief of whom be litavicus and he brother who be bear of a most noble family he share the bribe with they and exhort they to remember that they be free and bear for empire that the state of the aeduus be the only one which retard the most certain victory of the gaul that the rest be hold in check by its authority and if it be bring over the roman would not have room to stand on in gaul that he have receive some kindness from caesar only so far however as gain a most just cause by he decision but that he assign more weight to the general freedom for why should the aeduus go to caesar to decide concern they rights and law rather than the roman come to the aeduus the young man be easily win over by the speech of the magistrate and the bribe when they declare that they would even be leader in the plot a plan for accomplish it be consider because they be confident they state could not be induce to undertake the war on slight grounds it be resolve that litavicus should have the command of the ten thousand which be be send to caesar for the war and should have charge of they on they march and that he brother should go before he to caesar they arrange the other measure and the manner in which they should have they do xxxviii -- litavicus have receive the command of the army suddenly convene the soldier when he be about thirty mile distant from gergovium and weep say soldier whither be we go all we knight and all we noble have perish eporedorix and viridomarus the principal man of the state be accuse of treason have be slay by the roman without even permission to plead they cause learn this intelligence from those who have escape from the massacre for i since my brother and all my relation have be slay be prevent by grief from declare what have take place person be bring forward whom he have instruct in what he would have they say and make the same statement to the soldiery as litavicus have make : that all the knight of the aeduus be slay because they be say to have hold conference with the arvernus that they have conceal themselves among the multitude of soldier and have escape from the midst of the slaughter the aeduus shout aloud and conjure litavicus to provide for they safety as if say he it be a matter of we therefore if there be any spirit in we let we avenge the death of those who have perish in a most unworthy manner and let we slay these robber he point to the roman citizen who have accompany they in reliance on he protection he immediately seize a great quantity of corn and provision cruelly torture they and then put they to death send messenger throughout the entire state of the aeduus and eporedorix the aeduan a young man bear in the highest rank and possess very great influence at home and along with viridomarus of equal age and influence but of inferior birth whom caesar have raise from a humble position to the highest rank on be recommend to he by divitiacus have come in the number of horse be summon by caesar by name these have a dispute with each other for precedence and in through he kindness and after give three hour of the night to he army for he repose direct he march to gergovium almost in the middle of the journey a party of horse that be send by fabius state in how great danger matter be they inform he that the camp be attack by a very powerful army while fresh man be frequently relieve the wearied and exhausting we soldier by the incessant toil since on withstand they that fabius at they departure leave only two gate open be block up the rest and be add breast-works to the rampart and be prepare himself for a similar casualty on the follow day caesar after receive this information reach the camp before sunrise owing to the very great zeal of he soldier xlii -- whilst these thing be go on at gergovium the aeduus on receive the first announcement from litavicus leave themselves no time to ascertain the truth of these statement some be stimulate by avarice other by revenge and credulity which be a innate propensity in that race of man to such a degree that they consider a slight rumor as a ascertain fact they plunder the property of the roman citizen and either massacre they or drag they away to slavery convictolitani increase the evil state of affair and goad on the people to fury that by the commission of some outrage they may be ashamed to return to propriety they entice from the town of cabillonus by a promise of safety marcus aristius a military tribune who be on he march to he legion they compel those who have settle there for the purpose of trading to do the same by constantly attack they on they march they strip they of all they baggage they besiege day and night those that resist when many be slay on both side they excite a greater number to arm xliii -- in the meantime when intelligence be bring that all they property of litavicus and he brother they send ambassador to caesar for the purpose of clear themselves they do all this with a view to recover they soldier but be contaminate by guilt and charm by possibility of they be tear up have they branch only project from the ground there be five row in connection with and intersect each other and whoever enter within they be likely to impale themselves on very sharp stake the soldier call these cippus before these which be arrange in oblique row in the form of a quincunx pit three foot deep be dig which gradually diminish in depth to the bottom in these pit taper stake of the thickness of a man 's thigh sharpen at the top and harden in the fire be sink in such a manner as to project from the ground not more than four inch at the same time for the purpose of give they strength and stability they be each fill with trample clay to the height of one foot from the bottom : the rest of the pit be cover over with osier and twig to conceal the deceit eight row of this kind be dig and be three foot distant from each other they call this a lily from its resemblance to that flower stake a foot long with iron hook attach to they be entirely sink in the ground before these and be plant in every place at small interval these they call spur lxxiv -- after complete these work have select as level ground as he could consider the nature of the country and have enclose a area of fourteen mile he construct against a external enemy fortification of the same kind in every respect and separate from these so that the guard of the fortification they strength would support it the speech of critognatus ought not to be omit for its singular and detestable cruelty he spring from the noblest family among the arvernus and possess great influence say i shall pay no attention to the opinion of those who call a most disgraceful surrender by the name of a capitulation nor do i think that they ought to be consider as citizen or summon to the council my business be with those who approve of a sally : in whose advice the memory of we ancient prowess seem to dwell in the opinion of you all to be unable to bear privation for a short time be disgraceful cowardice not true valor those who voluntarily offer themselves to death be more easily find than those who would calmly endure distress and i would approve of this opinion -lrb- for honor baggage have advance to a considerable distance but caesar do not think it prudent to attack they when stand on they defense with such a steep hill in they favor nor keep he legion at such a distance that they could quit they post without danger : but perceive that he camp be divide from the enemy 's by a deep morass so difficult to cross that he could not pursue with expedition and that the hill beyond the morass which extend almost to the enemy 's camp be separate from it only by a small valley he lay a bridge over the morass and lead he army across and soon reach the plain on the top of the hill which be fortify on either side by a steep ascent have there draw up he army in order of battle he march to the furthest hill from which he could with he engine shower dart upon the thickest of the enemy xv -- the gaul confide in the natural strength of they position though they would not decline a engagement if the roman attempt to ascend the hill yet dare not divide they force into small party lest they should be throw into disorder by be disperse and therefore remain in order of battle caesar perceive that they persist in they resolution keep twenty cohort in battle array and measure out ground there for a camp order it to be fortify have complete he work he draw up he legion before the rampart and station the cavalry in certain position with they horse bridle when the bellovacus see the roman prepare to pursue they and that they could not wait the whole night or continue longer in the same place without provision they form the follow plan to secure a retreat they hand to one another the bundle of straw and stick on which they sit -lrb- for it be the custom of the gaul to sit when draw up in order of battle as have be assert in former commentary -rrb- of which they have great plenty in they camp and pile they in the front of they line and at the close of the day on a certain signal set they all on fire at one and the same time the continue blaze soon screen all they force from the sight of the roman which no sooner happen than the barbarian flee with the greatest precipitation xvi -- though caesar could not perceive the retreat of the enemy for the intervention of the fire yet suspect that they have adopt that method to favor they escape he make he legion advance and send a party of horse to pursue they but apprehensive of a ambuscade and that the enemy might remain in the same place and endeavor to draw we man into a disadvantageous situation he advance himself but slowly the horse be afraid to venture into the smoke and dense line of flame and those who be bold enough to attempt it be scarcely able to see they horse ' head give the enemy free liberty to retreat through fear of a ambuscade thus by a flight full at once of cowardice and address they advance without any loss about ten mile and encamp in a very strong position from which lay numerous ambuscade both of horse and foot they do considerable damage to the roman forager xvii -- after this have happen several time caesar discover from a certain prisoner that correus the general of the bellovacus have select six thousand of he bravest foot and a thousand horse with which he design to lie in ambush in a place to which he suspect the roman would send to look for forage on account of the abundance of corn and grass upon receive information of they design caesar draw out more legion than he usually do and send forward he cavalry as usual to protect the forager with these he intermix a guard of light infantry and himself advance with the legion as fast as he could xviii -- the gaul place in ambush have choose for the seat of action a level piece of bind not more than a mile in extent enclose on every side by a thick wood or a very deep river as by a toil and this they surround we man apprise of the enemy 's design march in good order to the ground ready both in heart and hand to give battle and willing to hazard any engagement when the legion be at they back on they approach as correus suppose that he have get a opportunity of effect he purpose he at first show himself with a small party and attack the foremost troops we man resolutely stand the charge and do not crowd together in one place as commonly happen from surprise in engagement between the horse whose number prove injurious to themselves xix -- when by the judicious arrangement of we force only a few of we man fight by turn and do not suffer themselves to be surround the rest of the enemy break out from the wood whilst correus be engage the battle be maintain in different part with great vigor and continue for a long time undecided till at length a body of foot gradually advance from the wood in order of battle and force we horse to give ground : the light infantry which be send before the legion to the assistance of the cavalry soon come up and mix with the horse fight with great courage the battle be for some time doubtful but as usually happen we man who stand the enemy 's first charge become superior from this very circumstance that though suddenly attack from a ambuscade they have sustain no loss in the meantime the legion be approach and several messenger arrive with notice to we man and the enemy that the -lrb- roman -rrb- general be near at hand with he force in battle array upon this intelligence we man confide in the support of the cohort fight most resolutely fear lest if they should be slow in they operation they should let the legion participate in the glory of the conquest the enemy lose courage and attempt to escape by different way in vain for they be themselves entangled in that labyrinth in which they think to entrap the roman be defeat and put to the rout and have lose the greater part of they man they flee in consternation whither-soever chance carry they some seek the wood other the river but be vigorously pursue by we man and put to the sword yet in the meantime correus unconquered by calamity could not be prevail on to quit the field and take refuge in the wood or accept we offer of quarter but fight courageously and wound several provoke we man elate with victory to discharge they weapon against he xx -- after this transaction caesar have come up immediately after the battle and imagine that the enemy upon receive the news of so great a defeat would be so depressed that they would abandon they camp which be not above eight mile distant from the scene of action though he see he passage obstruct by the river yet he march he army over and advanced but the bellovacus and the other state be inform of the loss caesar xxi -- this proposal have meet with general approbation comius the atrebatian flee to those german from whom he have borrow auxiliary for that war the rest instantly send ambassador to caesar usual clemency and mercy he never would have inflict that the power of the bellovacus be crush by the cavalry action that many thousand of they choicest foot have fall that scarce a man have escape to think by the submission of the rest that he know and be aware that the guilt of a crime be easily transfer to the dead but that no one person could have such influence as to be able by the feeble while caesar be hold the assizes in hither gaul titus labienus have discover that comius be tamper with the state and raise a conspiracy against caesar thought he might punish he infidelity without person may be leave in ignorance of the place where caesar and he army be at that time i have think proper to write a few word in addition to this commentary \* \* \* \* \* xlix -- caesar whilst in winter quarter in the country of the belgae make it he only business to keep the state in amity with he and to give none either hope of or pretext for a revolt for nothing be further from he wish than to be under the necessity of engage in another war at he departure lest when he be draw he army out of the country any war should be leave unfinished which the gaul would cheerfully undertake when already exhaust by so many unsuccessful battle -rrb- in obedience l -- when the winter quarter be break up he himself contrary to he usual practice proceed to italy by the longest possible stage in easily command the whole adriatic sea with the extremity of italy and the coast of greece and be able to conduct the war on either side of it or whether he remain there for want of shipping and be afraid that pompey would come to the conclusion that he ought not to relinquish italy he determine to deprive he of the means of communication afford by the harbor of brundusium the plan of he work be as follow : -- where the mouth of the port be narrowest he throw up a mole of earth on either side because in these place the sea be shallow have go out so far that the mole could not be continue in the deep water he fix double float thirty foot on either side before the mole these he fasten with four anchor at the four corner that they might not be carry away by the wave have complete and secure they he then join to they other float of equal size these he cover over with earth and mould that he might not be prevent from access to they to defend they and in the front and on both side he protect they with a parapet of wicker work and on every fourth one raise a turret two story high to secure they the better from be attack by the shipping and set on fire xxvi -- to counteract this pompey fit out large merchant ship which he find in the harbor of brundusium : on they he erect turret three story high and have furnish they with several engine and all sort of weapon drive they amongst caesar 's work to break through the float and interrupt the work thus there happen skirmish every day at a distance with sling arrow and other weapon caesar conduct matter as if he think that the hope of peace be not yet to be give up and though he be very much surprised that magius whom he have send to pompey with a message be not send back to he and though he attempt a reconciliation often retard the vigorous prosecution of he plan yet he think that he ought by all means to persevere in the same line of conduct he therefore send caninius rebilus to have a interview with scribonius libo he intimate friend and relation he charge he to exhort libo to effect a peace but above all thing require that he should be admit to a interview with pompey he declare that he have great hope if that be allow he that the consequence would be that both party would lay down they arm on equal term that a great share of the glory and reputation of that event would redound to libo if through he advice and agency hostility should be end libo have part from the conference with caninius go to pompey and shortly after return with answer that as the consul be absent no treaty of composition could be engage in without they caesar therefore think it time at length to give over the attempt which he have often make in vain and act with energy in the war xxvii -- when caesar 's work be nearly half finished and after nine day be spend in they the ship which have convey the first division of the army to dyrrachium be send back by the consul return to brundusium pompey either frighten at caesar 's work or determine from the begin to quit italy begin to prepare for he departure on the arrival of the ship and the more effectually to retard caesar 's attack lest he soldier should force they way into the town at the moment of he departure he stop up the gate build wall across the street and avenue sink trench across the way and in they fixed palisado and sharp stake which he make level with the ground by means of hurdle and clay but he barricade with large beam fasten in the ground and sharpen at the end two passage and road without the wall which lead to the port after make these arrangement he order he soldier to go on board without noise and dispose here and there on the wall and turret some light-armed veteran archer and slinger these he design to call off by a certain signal when all the soldier be embark and leave row-galley for they in a secure place xxviii -- the people of brundusium irritated by the insolence of pompey 's soldier and the insult receive from pompey himself be in favor of caesar 's party therefore as soon as they be aware of pompey 's departure whilst he man be run up and down and busy about they voyage they make sign from the top of the house : caesar be apprize of the design by they order scale ladder to be get ready and he man to take arm that he might not lose any opportunity of come to a action pompey weigh anchor at nightfall the soldier who have be post on the wall to guard it be call off by the signal which have be agree on and know the road run down to the ship caesar 's soldier fix they ladder and scale the wall : but be caution by the people to beware of the hidden stake and cover trench they halt and be conduct by the inhabitant by a long circuit they reach the port and capture with they long boat and small craft two of pompey 's ship full of soldier which have strike against caesar 's mole xxix-though caesar highly approve of collect a fleet and cross the sea and pursue pompey before he could strengthen himself with he transmarine auxiliary with the hope of bring the war to a conclusion yet he dread the delay and length of time necessary to effect it : because pompey by collect all he ship have deprive he of the means of pursue he at present the only resource leave to caesar be to wait for a fleet from the distant region of gaul picenum and the strait of gibraltar but this on account of the season of the year appear tedious and troublesome he be unwilling that in the meantime the veteran army and the two spain one of which be bind to pompey by the strongest obligation should be confirm in he interest that auxiliary and cavalry should be provide and gaul and italy reduce in he absence xxx -- therefore for the present he relinquish all intention of pursue pompey and resolve to march to spain and command the magistrate of the free town to procure he ship and to have they convey to brundusium he detach valerius he lieutenant with one legion to sardinium curio the proprietor to sicily with three legion and order he when he have recover sicily to immediately transport he army to africa marcus cotta be at this time governor of sardinium : marcus cato of sicily : and tubero by the lot should have have the government of africa the caralitanus as soon as they hear that valerius be send against they even before he leave italy of they own accord drive cotta out of the town who terrify because he understand that the whole province be combine -lrb- against he -rrb- flee from sardinium to africa cato be in sicily repair the old ship of war and demand new one from the state and these thing he perform with great zeal he be raise levy of roman citizen among the lucanus and brutius by he lieutenant and exact a certain quota of horse and foot from the state of sicily when these thing be nearly complete be inform of curio 's approach he make a complaint that he be abandon and betray by pompey who have undertake a unnecessary war without make any preparation and when question by he and other member in the senate have assure they that every thing be ready and provide for the war after have make these complaint in a public assembly he flee from he province xxxi -- valerius find sardinium and curio sicily desert by they governor when they arrive there with they army when tubero arrive in africa he find attius varus in the government of the province who have lose he people and country and he knowledge of that province he find the means of effect this because a few year before at the expiration of he praetorship he have obtain that province he when tubero come to affair be despatch caesar that there might be a intermission from labor for the rest of the season draw off he soldier to the nearest municipal town and set off in person for rome have assemble the senate he remind they of the injustice of he enemy and tell they that he aim at no extraordinary honor but have wait for the time appoint by law for stand candidate for the consulate be contented with what be allow to every citizen that a bill have be carry by the ten tribune of the people -lrb- notwithstanding the resistance of he enemy and a very violent opposition from cato who in he usual manner consume the day by a tedious harangue -rrb- that he should be allow to stand candidate though absent even in the consulship of pompey and if the latter disapprove of the bill why do he allow it to pass if he approve of it why should he debar he -lrb- caesar -rrb- from the people 's favor he make mention of he own patience in that he have freely propose that all army should be disband by which he himself would suffer the loss both of dignity and honor he urge the virulence of he enemy who refuse to comply with what they require from other and have rather that all thing should be throw into confusion than that they should lose they power and they army he expatiate on they injustice in take away he legion : they cruelty and insolence in abridge the privilege of the tribune the proposal he have make and he entreaty of a interview which have be refuse he : for which reason he beg and desire that they would undertake the management of the republic and unite with he in the administration of it but if through fear they decline it he would not be a burden to they but take the management of it on himself that deputy ought to be send to pompey to propose a reconciliation as he do not regard what pompey have lately assert in the senate that authority be acknowledge to be vest in those person to whom ambassador be send and fear imply in those that send they that these be the sentiment of low weak mind : that for he part as he have make it he study to surpass other in glory so he be desirous of excel they in justice and equity xxxiii -- the senate approve of send deputy but none could be find fit to execute the commission : for every person from he own private fear decline the office for pompey on leave the city have declare in the open senate that he would hold in the same degree of estimation those who stay in rome and those in caesar 's camp thus three day be waste in dispute and excuse besides lucius metellus one of the tribune be suborn by caesar 's enemy to prevent this and to embarrass everything else which caesar should propose caesar have discover he intention after spend several day to no purpose leave the city in order that he might not lose any more time and go to transalpine gaul without effect what he have intend xxxiv -- on he arrival there he be inform that vibullius rufus whom he have take a few day before at corfinium and set at liberty be send by pompey into spain and that domitius also be go to seize massilium with seven row-galley which be fit up by some private person at igilium and cosa and which he have man with he own slave freedman and colonist : and that some young nobleman of massilium have be send before he whom pompey when leave rome have exhort that the late service of caesar should not erase from they mind the memory of he former favor on receive this message the massilian have shut they gate against caesar and invite over to they the albicus who have formerly be in alliance with they and who that they ought to follow the precedent set by all italy rather than submit to the will of any one man he make use of such argument as he think would tend to bring they to reason the deputy report he speech to they countryman and by the authority of the state bring he back this answer : that they understand that the roman people be divide into two faction : that they have neither judgment nor ability to decide which have the juster cause but that the head of these faction be cneius pompey and caius caesar the two patron of the state : the former of whom have grant to they state the land of the volcae arecomici and helvii the latter have assign they a part of he conquest in gaul and have augment they revenue wherefore have receive equal favor from both they ought to show equal affection to both and assist neither against the other nor admit either into they city or harbor xxxvi -- whilst this treaty be go forward domitius arrive at massilium with he fleet and be receive into the city and make governor of it the chief management of the war be entrust to he at he command they send the fleet to all part they seize all the merchantman they could meet with and carry they into the harbor they apply the nail timber and rig with which they be furnish to rig and refit they other vessel they lay up in the public store all the corn that be find in the ship and reserve the rest of they lading and convoy for the siege of the town should such a event take place provoke at such ill treatment caesar lead three legion against massilium and resolve to provide turret and vina to by letter and messenger he have make two bridge over the river segre at the distance of four mile from each other he send forage party over these bridge because he have already consume all the forage that be on he side of the river the general of pompey 's army do almost the same thing and for the same reason : and the horse have frequent skirmish with each other when two of fabius 's legion have as be they constant practice go forth as the usual protection to the forager and have cross the river and the baggage and all the horse be follow they on a sudden from the weight of the cattle and the he own bridge which communicate between he camp and the town with four legion and all the cavalry and march against fabius 's two legion when he approach be announce lucius plancus who have the command of those legion compel by the emergency take post on a rise ground and draw up he army with two front that it might not be surround by the cavalry thus though engage with superior number he sustain the furious charge of the legion and the horse when the battle be begin by the horse there be observe at a distance by both side the color of two legion which caius fabius have send round by the further bridge to reinforce we man suspect as the event verify that the enemy 's general would take advantage of the opportunity which fortune have put in they way to attack we man they approach put a end to the battle and each general lead back he legion to they respective camp xli -- in two day after caesar come to the camp with nine hundred horse which he have retain for a bodyguard the camp and all he baggage and the next day set off in person for ilerda with all he force draw up in three line and halt just before the camp of afranius and have remain there a short time under arm he
