resolve to encamp at somewhat less than half a mile 's distance from the very foot of the mountain and that he soldier whilst engage in they work might not be terrify by any sudden attack of the enemy or disturb in they work he order they not to fortify it with a wall which must rise high and be see at a distance but draw on the front opposite the enemy a trench fifteen foot broad the first and second line continue under arm as be from the first appoint behind they the third line be carry on the work without be see so that the whole be complete before afranius discover that the camp be be fortify xlii -- in the evening caesar draw he legion within this trench and rest they under arm the next night the day follow he keep he whole army within it and as it be necessary to bring material from a considerable distance he for the present pursue the same plan in he work and to each legion one after the other he assign one side of the camp to fortify and order trench of the same magnitude to be cut : he keep the rest of the legion under arm without baggage to oppose the enemy afranius and petreius to frighten we and obstruct the work draw out they force at the very foot of the mountain and challenge we to battle caesar however do not interrupt he work rely on the protection of the three legion and the strength of the fosse after stay for a short time and advance no great distance from the bottom of the hill they lead back they force to they camp the third day caesar fortify he camp with a rampart and order the other cohort which he have leave in the upper camp and he baggage to be remove to it xliil-between the town of ilerda and the next hill on which afranius and petreius be encamp there be a plain about three hundred pace broad and near the middle of it a eminence somewhat raise above the level : caesar hope that if he could get possession of this and fortify it he should be able to cut off the enemy from the town the bridge and all the store which they have lay up in the town in expectation of this he lead three legion out of the camp and draw up he army in a advantageous position he order the advanced man of one legion to hasten forward and seize the eminence upon intelligence of this the cohort which be on guard before afranius 's camp be instantly send a nearer way to occupy the same post the two party engage and as afranius 's man have reach the eminence first we man be repulse and on a reinforcement be send they be oblige to turn they back and retreat to the standard of legion xliv -- the manner of fighting of those soldier be to run forward with great impetuosity and boldly take a post and not to keep they rank strictly but to fight in small scatter party : if hard press they think it no disgrace to retire and give up the post be accustom to this manner of fighting among the lusitanian and other barbarous nation for it commonly happen that soldier be strongly influence by the custom of those country in which they have spend much time this method however alarm we man who be not use to such a description of warfare for they imagine that they be about to be surround on they expose flank by the single man who run forward from they rank and they think it they duty to keep they rank and not to quit they color nor without good reason to give up the post which they have take accordingly when the advanced guard give way the legion which be station on that wing do not keep its ground but retreat to the next hill xlv -- almost the whole army be daunt at this because it have occur contrary to they expectation and custom caesar encourage he man and lead the ninth legion to they relief and check the insolent and eager pursuit of the enemy and oblige they in they turn to show they back and retreat to ilerda and take post under the wall but the soldier of the ninth legion be over zealous to repair the dishonor which have be sustained have rashly pursue the flee enemy advance into disadvantageous ground and go up to the foot of the mountain on which the town ilerda be build and when they wish to retire they be again attack by the enemy from the rise ground the place be craggy in the front and steep on either side and be so narrow that even three cohort draw up in order of battle would fill it but no relief could be send on the flank and the horse could be of no service to they when hard press from the town indeed the precipice incline with a gentle slope for near four hundred pace we man have to retreat this way as they have through they eagerness advance too inconsiderately the greatest contest be in this place which be much to the disadvantage of we troops both on account of its narrowness and because they be post at the foot of the mountain so that no weapon be throw at they without effect : yet they exert they valor and patience and bear every wound the enemy 's force be increase and cohort be frequently send to they aid from the camp through the town that fresh man might relieve the weary caesar be oblige to do the same and relieve the fatigue by send cohort to that post xlvi -- after the battle have in this manner continue incessantly for five hour and we man have suffer much from superior number have spend all they javelin they draw they sword and charge the enemy up the hill and have kill a few oblige the rest to fly the cohort be beat back to the wall and some be drive by they fear into the town a easy retreat be afford to we man we cavalry also on either flank though station on sloping or low ground yet bravely struggle up to the top of the hill and ride between the two army make we retreat more easy and secure such be the various turn of fortune in the battle in the first encounter about seventy of we man fall : amongst they quintus fulgenius first centurion of the second line of the fourteenth legion who for he extraordinary valor have be promote from the lower rank to that post about six hundred be wound of afranius 's party there be kill titus caecilius principal centurion and four other centurion and above two hundred man xlvii -- but this opinion be spread abroad concern this day that each party think that they come off conqueror afranius 's soldier because though they be esteem inferior in the opinion of all yet they have stand we attack and sustain we charge and at first have keep the post and the hill which have be the occasion of the dispute and in the first encounter have oblige we man to fly : but ours because notwithstanding the disadvantage of the ground and the disparity of number they have maintain the battle for five hour have advance up the hill sword in hand and have force the enemy to fly from the higher ground and drive they into the town the enemy fortify the hill about which the contest have be with strong work and post a garrison on it xlviii -- in two day after this transaction there happen a unexpected misfortune for so great a storm arise that it be agree that there be never see higher flood in those country it sweep down the snow from all the mountain and break over the bank of the river and in one day carry away both the bridge which fabius have build -- a circumstance which cause great difficulty to caesar 's army for as we camp as already mention be pitch between two river the segre and cinca and as neither of these could be ford for the space of thirty mile they be all of necessity confine within these narrow limit neither could the state which have espouse caesar 's cause furnish he with corn nor the troops which have go far to forage return as they be stop by the water : nor could the convoy come from italy and gaul make they way to the camp besides it be the most distressing season of the year when there be no corn in the blade and it be nearly ripe : and the state be exhaust because afranius have convey almost all the corn before caesar 's arrival into ilerda and whatever he have leave have be already consume by caesar the cattle which might have serve as the targeteer of hither spain who be well acquaint with the country and could readily swim across the river because it be the custom of all those people not to join they army without bladder xlix -- but afranius 's army have abundance of everything a great stock of corn have be provide and lay in long before a large quantity be come in from the whole province : they have a good store of forage the bridge of ilerda afford a opportunity of get all these without any danger and the place beyond the bridge to which caesar have no access be as yet untouched l -- those flood continue several day caesar endeavor to repair the bridge but the height of the water do not allow he : and the cohort dispose along the bank do not suffer they to be complete and it be easy for they to prevent it both from the nature of the river and the height of the water but especially because they dart be throw from the whole course of the bank on one confine spot and it be no easy matter at one and the same time to execute a work in a very rapid flood and to avoid the dart li -- intelligence be bring to afranius that the great convoy which be on they march to caesar have halt at the river archer from the ruthenus and horse from the gaul with a long train of baggage accord to the gallic custom of travel have arrive there there be besides about six thousand people of all description with slave and free man but there be no order or regular discipline as every one follow he own humor and all travel without apprehension take the same liberty as on former march there be several young nobleman son of senator and of equestrian rank there be ambassador from several state there be lieutenant of caesar 's the river stop they all to attack they by surprise afranius set out in the beginning of the night with all he cavalry and three legion and send the horse on before to fall on they unawares but the gallic horse soon get themselves in readiness and attack they though but few they withstand the vast importance to the security of we man for have gain time they retire to the higher grounds there be miss that day about two hundred bow-man a few horse and a inconsiderable number of servant and baggage lii -- however by all these thing the price of provision be raise which be commonly a disaster attendant not only on a time of present scarcity but on the apprehension of future want provision have now reach fifty denarius each bushel and the want of corn have diminish the strength of the soldier and the inconvenience be increase every day : and so great a alteration be work in a few day and fortune have so changed side that we man have to struggle with the want of every necessary while the enemy have a abundant supply of all thing and be consider to have the advantage caesar demand from those state which have accede to he alliance a supply of cattle as they have but little corn he send away the camp follower to the more distant state and endeavor to remedy the present scarcity cneius pompey some of they to be the first to bring he the intelligence other that they might not be think to have wait the issue of the war and to have come last of all liv -- when caesar 's affair be in this unfavourable position and all the pass be guard by the soldier and horse of afranius and the bridge could not be prepared caesar order he soldier to make ship of the kind that he knowledge of britain a few year before have teach he first the keel and rib be make of light timber then the rest of the hulk of the ship be work with wicker-work and cover over with hide when these be finish he draw they down to the river in waggon in one night a distance of twenty-two mile from he camp and transport in they some soldier across the river and on a sudden take possession of a hill adjoining the bank this he immediately fortify before he be perceive by the enemy to this he afterwards transport a legion : and have begin a bridge on both side he finish it in two day by this mean he bring forager by surprise as they be disperse without any suspicion intercept a incredible number of cattle and people and when some spanish light-armed cohort be send to reinforce the enemy we man judiciously divide themselves into two part the one to protect the spoil the other to resist the advance foe and to beat they back and they cut off from the rest and surround one cohort which have rashly venture out of the line before the other and after put it to the sword return safe with considerable booty to the camp over the same bridge lvi -- whilst these affair be go forward at ilerda the massilian adopt the advice of domitius prepared seventeen ship of war of which eleven be deck to these they add several smaller vessel that we fleet might be terrify by number : they man they with a great number of archer and of the albicus of whom mention have be already make and these they incite by reward and promise domitius require certain ship for he own use which he man with colonist and massilia lvii -- brutus be much inferior in number of ship but caesar have appoint to that fleet the bravest man select from all he legion antesignanus and centurion who have request to be employ in that service they have provide iron hook and harpoon and have furnish themselves with a vast number of javelin dart and missile thus prepared and be apprise of the enemy 's approach they put out from the harbor and engage the massilian both side fight with great courage and resolution nor do the albicus a hardy people breed on the highland and inure to arm fall much short of we man in valor : and be lately come from the massilian they retain in they mind they recent promise : and the wild shepherd encourage by the hope of liberty be eager to prove they zeal in the presence of they master lviii -- the massilian themselves confide in the quickness of they ship and the skill of they pilot elude ours and evade the shock and as long as they be permit by clear space lengthen they line they endeavor to surround we or to attack single ship with several of theirs or to run across we ship and carry away we oar if possible but when necessity oblige they to come nearer they have recourse from the skill and art of the pilot to the valor of the mountaineer but we man not have such expert seaman or skilful pilot for they have be hastily draft from the merchant ship and be not yet acquaint even with the name of the rigging be moreover impede by the heaviness and slowness of we vessel which have be build in a hurry and of green timber be not so easily manoeuvre therefore when caesar 's man have a opportunity of a close engagement they cheerfully oppose two of the enemy 's ship with one of theirs and throw in the grapple iron and hold both ship fast they fight on both side of the deck and board the enemy 's and have kill number of the albicus and shepherd they sink some of they ship take other with the man on board and drive the rest into the harbor that day the massilian lose nine ship include those that be take lix -- when news of this battle be bring to caesar at ilerda the bridge be complete at the same time fortune soon take a turn the enemy daunt by the courage of we horse do not scour the country as freely or as boldly as before : but sometimes advance a small distance from the camp that they might have a ready retreat they forage within narrower bound : at other time they take a longer circuit to avoid we outpost and party of horse or have sustain some loss or descry we horse at a distance they flee in the midst of they expedition leave they baggage behind they at length they resolve to leave off forage for several day and contrary to the practice of all nation to go out at night lx -- in the meantime the oscens and the calagurritanus who be under the 's name be not know to the barbarian from these they expect considerable aid both of horse and foot and hope to protract the war till winter in a friendly country have come to this resolution they caesar encourage by they zeal and importunity though he feel reluctant to expose he army to a river so exceedingly large yet judge it prudent to attempt it and make a trial accordingly he order all be make from caesar 's camp lucius decidius saxa be detach with a small party to explore the nature of the country each return with the same account to he camp that there be a level road for the next they duty wherefore they should by all mean attempt to force they way by day for though a trifling loss might be sustained yet the post which they desire might be secure with safety to the main body town iii -- in the meantime lucius nasidius be send by cneius pompey with a fleet of sixteen sail a few of which have beak of brass to the assistance of lucius domitius and the massilian pass the they internal resource or by foreign assistance vi -- when the battle be begin no effort of valor be want to the massilian but mindful of the instruction which they have a little before receive from they friend they fight with such spirit as if they suppose that they would never have another opportunity to attempt a defense and as if they believe that those whose life should be endanger in the battle would not long precede the fate of the rest of the citizen who if the city be take must undergo the same fortune of war we ship be at some distance from each other room be allow both for the skill of they pilot and the manoeuvring of they ship and if at any time ours gain a advantage by cast the iron hook on board they ship grapple with they from all part they assist those who be distressed nor after be join by the albicus do they decline come to close engagement nor be they much inferior to we man in valor at the same time shower of dart throw from a distance from the lesser ship suddenly inflict several wound on we man when off they guard and otherwise engage and two of they three-decked galley have descry the ship of decimus brutus which could be easily distinguish by its flag row up against he with great violence from opposite side : but brutus see into they design by the swiftness of he ship extricate himself with such address as to get clear though only by a moment from the velocity of they motion they strike against each other with such violence that they be both excessively injure by the shock the beak indeed of one of they be break off the whole ship be ready to founder which circumstance be observe the ship of brutus 's fleet which be nearest that station attack they when in this disorder and sink they both vii -- but nasidius 's ship be of no use and soon leave the fight for the sight of they country or the entreaty of they relation do not urge they to run a desperate risk of they life therefore of the number of the ship not one be lose : of the fleet of the massilian five be sink four take and one run off with nasidius : all that escape make the best of they way to hither spain but one of the rest be send forward to massilia for the purpose of bear this intelligence and when it come near the city the whole people crowd out to hear the tiding and on be inform of the event be so oppressed with grief that one would have imagine that the city have be take by a enemy at the same moment the massilian however begin to make the necessary preparation for the defense of they city with unwearied energy viii -- the legionary soldier who have the management of the work on the right side observe from the frequent sally of the enemy that it might prove a great protection to they to build a turret of brick under the wall for a fort and place of refuge which they at first build low and small -lrb- to guard they -rrb- against sudden attack to it they retreat and from it they make defense if any superior force attack they and from it they sally out either to repel or pursue the enemy it extend thirty foot on every side and the thickness of the wall be five foot but afterwards as experience be the best master in everything on which the wit of man be employ it be find that it might be of considerable service if it be raise to the usual height of turret which be effect in the follow manner ix-when the turret be raise to the height for flooring they lay it on the wall in such a manner that the end of the joist be cover by the outer face of the wall that nothing should project to which the enemy 's fire might adhere they moreover build over the joist with small brick as high as the protection of the pluteus and vinea permit they and on that place they lay two beam across angle-way at a small distance from the outer wall to support the rafter which be to cover the turret and on the beam they lay joist across in a direct line and on these they fasten down plank these joist they make somewhat longer to project beyond the outside of the wall that they might serve to hang a curtain on they to defend and repel all blow whilst they be build the wall between that and the next floor and the floor of this story they face with brick and mortar that the enemy 's fire might do they no damage and on this they spread mattress lest the weapon throw from engine should break through the flooring or stone from catapult should batter the brickwork they moreover make three mat of cable rope each of they the length of the turret wall and four foot broad and hang they round the turret on the three side which face the enemy fasten they to the project joist for this be the only sort of defense which they have learn by experience in other place could not be pierce by dart or engine but when that part of the turret which be complete be protect and secure against every attempt of the enemy they remove the pluteus to other work they begin to suspend gradually and raise by screw from the first-floor the entire roof of the turret and then they elevate it as high as the length of the mat allow hide and secure within these covering they build up the wall with brick and again by another turn of the screw clear a place for themselves to proceed with the building and when they think it time to lay another floor they lay the end of the beam cover in by the outer brick in like manner as in the first story and from that story they again raise the uppermost floor and the mat-work in this manner securely and without a blow or danger they raise it six story high and in lay the material leave loop-hole in such place as they think proper for work they engine x -- when they be confident that they could protect the work which lay around from this turret they resolve to build a musculus sixty foot long of timber two foot square and to extend it from the brick tower to the enemy 's tower and wall this be the form of it : two beam of equal length be lay on the ground at the distance of four foot from each other and in they be fasten small pillar five foot high which be join together by brace with a gentle slope on which the timber which they must place to support the roof of the musculus should be lay : upon this be lay beam two foot square bind with iron plate and nail to the upper covering of the musculus and the upper beam they fasten lath four finger square to support the tile which be to cover the musculus the roof be thus sloped and lay over in row in the same manner as the joist be lay on the brace the musculus be cover with tile and mortar to secure it against fire which might be throw from the wall over the tile hide be spread to prevent the water let in on they by spout from dissolve the cement of the brick again the hide be cover over with mattress that they might not be destroy by fire or stone the soldier under the protection of the vinea finish this whole work to the very tower and suddenly before the enemy be aware of it move it forward by naval machinery by put roller under it close up to the enemy 's turret so that it even touch the building xi -- the townsman affright at this unexpected stroke bring forward with lever the largest stone they can procure and pitch they from the wall roll they down on the musculus the strength of the timber withstand the shock and whatever fall on it slide off on account of the sloping roof when they perceive this they alter they plan and set fire to barrel fill with resin and tar and roll they down from the wall on the musculus as soon as they fall on it they slide off again and be remove from its side by long pole and fork in the meantime the soldier under cover of the musculus be looting out with crowbar the lowest stone of the enemy 's turret with which the foundation be lay the musculus be defend by dart throw from engine by we man from the brick tower and the enemy be beat off from the wall and turret nor be a fair opportunity of defend the wall give they at length several stone be pick away from the foundation of that turret next the musculus part of it fall down suddenly and the rest as if follow it lean forward xii -- hereupon the enemy distressed at the sudden fall of the turret surprise at the unforeseen calamity awed by the wrath of the god and dread the pillage of they city rush all together out of the gate unarmed with they temple bind with fillet and suppliantly stretch out they hand to the officer and the army at this uncommon occurrence the whole progress of the war be stop and the soldier turn away from the battle run eagerly to hear and listen to they when the enemy come up to the commander and the army they all fall down at they foot and besought they to wait till caesar 's arrival they see that they city be take we work complete and they tower undermine therefore they desist from a defense that no obstacle could arise to prevent they be instantly plunder at a beck as soon as he arrive if they refuse to submit to he order they inform they that if the turret have entirely fall down the soldier could not be withhold from force into the town and sack it in hope of get spoil these and several other argument to the same effect be deliver as they be a people of great learning with great pathos and lamentation xiii -- the lieutenant move with compassion draw off the soldier from the work desist from the assault and leave sentinel on the work a sort of a truce have be make through compassion for the besiege the arrival of caesar be anxiously await not a dart be throw from the wall or by we man but all remit they care and diligence as if the business be at a end for caesar have give trebonius strict charge not to suffer the town to be take by storm lest the soldier too much irritated both by abhorrence of they revolt by the contempt show to they and by they long labor should put to the sword all the grown-up inhabitant as they threaten to do and it be with difficulty that they be then restrain from break into the town and they be much displeased because they imagine that they be prevent by trebonius from take possession of it xiv -- but the enemy destitute of all honor only wait a time and opportunity for fraud and treachery and after a interval of some day when we man be careless and negligent on a sudden at noon when some be disperse and other indulge themselves in rest on the very work after the fatigue of the day and they arm be all lay by and cover up they sally out from the gate and the wind be high and favourable to they they set fire to we work and the wind spread it in such a manner that in the same instant the agger plutei testudo tower and engine all catch the flame and be consume before we could conceive how it have occur we man alarm at such a unexpected turn of fortune lay hold on such arm as they could find some rush from the camp a attack be make on the enemy : but they be prevent by arrow and engine from the wall from pursue they when they flee they retire to they wall and there without fear set the musculus and brick tower on fire thus by the perfidy of the enemy and the violence of the storm the labor of many month be destroy in a moment the massilian make the same attempt the next day have get such another storm they sally out against the other tower and agger and fight with more confidence but as we man have on the former occasion give up all thought of a contest so warn by the event of the precede day they have make every preparation for a defense accordingly they slew several and force the rest to retreat into the town without effect they design xv -- trebonius begin to provide and repair what have be destroy with much greater zeal on the part of the soldier for when they see that they extraordinary pain and preparation have a unfortunate issue they be fire with indignation that in consequence of the impious violation of the truce they valor should be hold in derision there be no place leave they from which the material for they mound could be fetch in consequence of all the timber far and wide in the territory of the massilian have be cut down and carry away they begin therefore to make a agger of a new construction never hear of before of two wall of brick each six foot thick and to lay floor over they of almost the same breadth with the agger make of timber but wherever the space between the wall or the weakness of the timber seem to require it pillar be place underneath and traverse beam lay on to strengthen the work and the space which be floor be cover over with hurdle and the hurdle plaster over with mortar the soldier cover overhead by the floor on the right and leave by the wall and in the front by the mantlet carry whatever material be necessary for the building without danger : the business be soon finish -- the loss of they laborious work be soon repair by the dexterity and fortitude of the soldier gate for make sally be leave in the wall in such place as they think proper xvi -- but when the enemy perceive that those work which they have hope could not be replace without a great length of time be put into so thorough repair by a few day ' labor and diligence that there be no room for perfidy or sally and that no means be leave they by which they could either hurt the man by resistance or the work by fire and when they find by former example that they town could be surround with a wall and turret on every part by which it be accessible by land in such a manner that they could not have room to stand on they own fortification because we work be build almost on the top of they wall by we army and dart could be throw from we hand and when they perceive that all advantage arise from they engine on which they have build great hope be totally lose and that though they have a opportunity of fight with we on equal term from wall and turret they could perceive that they be not equal to we man in bravery they have recourse to the same proposal of surrender as before xvii -- in further spain marcus varro in the beginning of the disturbance when he hear of the circumstance which take place in italy be diffident of pompey 's success use to speak in a very friendly manner of caesar that though be pre-engaged to cneius pompey in quality of lieutenant he be bind in honor to he that nevertheless there exist a very intimate tie between he and caesar that he be not ignorant of what be the duty of a lieutenant who bear a office of trust nor of he own strength nor of the disposition of the whole province to caesar these sentiment he constantly express in he ordinary conversation and do not attach himself to either party but afterwards when he find that caesar be detain before massilium that the force of petreius have effect a junction with the army of afranius that considerable reinforcement have come to they assistance that there be great hope and expectation and hear that the whole hither province have enter into a confederacy and of the difficulty to which caesar be reduce afterwards at ilerda for want of provision and afranius write to he a fuller and more exaggerated account of these matter he begin to regulate he movement by those of fortune xviii -- he make levy throughout the province and have complete he two legion he add to they about thirty auxiliary cohort : he collect a large quantity of corn to send partly to the massilian partly to afranius and petreius he command the inhabitant of gade to build ten ship of war besides he take care that several other should be build in spain he remove all the money and ornament from the temple of hercule to the town of gade and send six cohort thither from the province to guard they and give the command of the town of gade to caius gallonius a roman knight and friend of domitius who have come thither send by domitius to recover a estate for he and he deposit all the arm both public and private in gallonius 's house he himself -lrb- varro -rrb- make severe harangue against caesar he often pronounce from he tribunal that caesar have fight several unsuccessful battle and that a great number of he man have desert to afranius that he have these account from undoubted messenger and authority on which he could rely by these means he terrify the roman citizen of that province and oblige they to promise he for the service of the state one hundred and ninety thousand sesterce twenty thousand pound weight of silver and a hundred and twenty thousand bushel of wheat he lay heavier burden on those state which he think be friendly disposed to caesar and billet troops on they he pass judgment against some private person and condemn to confiscation the property of those who have speak or make oration against the republic and force the whole province to take a oath of allegiance to he and pompey be inform of all that happen in hither spain he prepare for war this be he plan of operation he be to retire with he two legion to gade and to lay up all the shipping and provision there for he have be inform that the whole province be incline to favor caesar 's party he think that the war might be easily protracted in a island if he be provide with corn and shipping caesar although call back to italy by many and important matter yet have determine to leave no dregs of war behind he in spain because he know that pompey have many dependant and client in the hither province xix -- have therefore send two legion into further spain under the command of quintus cassius tribune of the people he himself advance with six hundred horse by force march and issue a proclamation appoint a day on which the magistrate and nobility of all the state should attend he at corduba this proclamation be publish through the whole province there be not a state that do not send a part of they senate to corduba at the appoint time and not a roman citizen of any note but appear that day at the same time the senate at corduba shut the gate of they own accord against varro and post guard and sentinel on the wall and in the turret and detain two cohort -lrb- call colonica which have come there accidentally -rrb- for the defense of the town about the same time the people of carmona which be by far the strongest state in the whole province of themselves drive out of the town the cohort and shut the gate against they although three cohort have be detach by varro to garrison the citadel xx -- but varro be in greater haste on this account to reach gade with he legion as soon as possible lest he should be stop either on he march or on cross over to the island the affection of the province to caesar prove so great and so favourable that he receive a letter from gade before he be far advance on he march : that as soon as the nobility of gade hear of caesar 's proclamation they have combine with the tribune of the cohort which be in garrison there to drive gallonius out of the town and to secure the city and island for caesar that have agree on the design they have send notice to gallonius to quit gade of he own accord whilst he could do it with safety if he do not they would take measure for themselves that for fear of this gallonius have be induce to quit the town when this be know one of varro 's two legion which be call there approve so highly of this act that every one most earnestly offer to entertain they in they house when varro terrify at these thing have alter he route propose go to italica he be inform by he friend that the gate be shut against he then indeed when intercept from every road he send word to caesar that he be ready to deliver up the legion which he command he send to he sextus caesar and order he to deliver it up to he varro have deliver up the legion go to caesar to corduba and have lay before he the public account hand over to he most faithfully whatever money he have and tell he what quantity of corn and shipping he have and where xxi -- caesar make a public oration at corduba in which he return thanks to all severally : to the roman citizen because they have be zealous to keep the town in they own power to the spaniard for have drive out the garrison to the gaditanus for have defeat the attempt of he enemy and assert they own liberty to the tribune and centurion who to narbo and thence to massilium there he be inform that a law be pass for create a dictator and that he have be nominate dictator by marcus lepidus the praetor xxii -- the massilian weary out by misfortune of every sort reduce to the lowest ebb for want of corn conquer in two engagement at sea defeat in they frequent sally and struggle moreover with a fatal pestilence from they long confinement and change of victuals -lrb- for they all subsist on old millet and damaged barley which they have formerly provide and lay up in the public store against a emergency of this kind -rrb- they turret be demolish a great part of they wall have give way and despairing of any aid either from the province or they army for these they have hear have fall into caesar 's power resolve to surrender now without dissimulation but a few day before lucius domitius have discover the intention of the massilian and have procure three ship two of which he give up to he friend go on board the third himself have get a brisk wind put out to sea some ship which by brutus 's order be constantly cruise near the port have espy he weigh anchor and pursue he but of these the ship on board of which he be persevere itself and continue its flight and by the aid of the wind get out of sight : the other two affright by the approach of we galley put back again into the harbor the massilian convey they arm and engine out of the town as they be order : bring they ship out of the port and dock and deliver up the money in they treasury when these affair be despatch caesar spare the town more out of regard to they renown and antiquity than to any claim they could lay to he favor leave two legion in garrison there send the rest to italy and set out himself for rome xxiii -- about the same time caius curio have sail from sicily to africa and from the first despise the force of publius attius varus transport only two of the four legion which he have receive from caesar and five hundred horse and have spend two day and three night on the voyage arrive at a place call aquilarium which be about twenty-two mile distant from clupea and in the summer season have a convenient harbor and be enclose by two project promontory lucius caesar the son who be wait he arrival near clupea with ten ship which have be take near utica in a war with the pirate and which publius attius have have repair for this war frighten at the number of we ship flee the sea and run he three-decked covered galley on the nearest shore leave she there and make he escape by land to adrumetum caius considius longus with a garrison of one legion guard this town the rest of caesar 's fleet after he flight retire to adrumetum marcus rufus the quaestor pursue he with twelve ship which curio have bring from sicily as convoy to the merchantman and see a ship leave on the shore he bring she off by a tow rope and return with he fleet to curio xxiv -- curio detach marcus before with the fleet to utica and march thither with he army have advance two day he come to the river bagrada and there leave caius caninius rebilus the lieutenant with the legion and go forward himself with the horse to view the cornelian camp because that be reckon a very eligible position for encamp it be a straight ridge project into the sea steep and rough on both side but the ascent be more gentle on that part which lie opposite utica it be not more than a mile distant from utica in a direct line but on this road there be a spring to which the sea come up and overflow a extensive morass be thereby form and if a person would avoid it he must make a circuit of six mile to reach the town xxv -- have examine this place curio get a view of varus 's camp join the wall and town at the gate call bellica well fortify by its natural situation on one side by the town itself on the other by a theater which be before the town the approach to the town be render difficult and narrow by the very extensive out-building of that structure at the same time he observe the road very full of carriage and cattle which they be convey from the country into the town on the sudden alarm he send he cavalry after they to plunder they and get the spoil and at the same time varus have detach as a guard for they six hundred numidian horse and four hundred foot which king juba have send to utica as auxiliary a few day before there be a friendship subsist between he -lrb- juba 's -rrb- father and pompey and a feud between he and curio because he when a tribune of the people have propose a law in which he endeavor to make the army with plenty of everything xxvi -- after these transaction curio return to he camp at bagrada and by a general shout of the whole army be salute imperator the next day he lead he army to utica and encamp near the town before the work of the camp be finish the horse upon guard bring he word that a large supply of horse and foot send by king juba be on they march to utica and at the same time a cloud of dust be observe and in a moment the front of the line be in sight curio surprise at the suddenness of the affair send on the horse to receive they first charge and detain they he be throw into disorder and confusion because they have march without any order and be under no apprehension betake themselves to flight : almost all the enemy 's horse be safe because they make a curio 's camp to attius varus they whether they utter the sentiment which they really entertain or wish to gratify varus -lrb- for what we wish we readily give credit to and what we think ourselves we -- in varus 's army there be one sextus quintilius varus who as we have mention before be at corfinium when caesar give he he liberty he go over to africa now curio have transport to africa those opinion of he own and to what he have hear from other add he own apprehension when this have spread from a single author to several person and be hand from one another there appear to be many author for such sentiment as these : -lrb- that it be a civil war that they be man and therefore that it be lawful for they to act freely and follow which party they please these be the legion which a short proceed from the marsus and pelignus as those which pass in the tent the night before and some of they fellow soldier hear they with displeasure some addition be also make to they by those who wish to be think more zealous in they duty -rrb- xxx -- for these reason have call a council curio begin to deliberate on the general welfare there be some opinion which advise by all mean a attempt to be make and a attack on varus 's camp for when such sentiment prevail among the soldier they think idleness be improper in short they say that it be better bravely to try the hazard of war in a battle than to be desert and surround by they own troops and force to submit to the greatest cruelty there be some who give they opinion that they ought to withdraw at the third watch to the cornelian camp that by a longer interval of time the soldier might be bring to a proper way of thinking and also that if any misfortune should befall they they might have a safer and readier retreat to sicily from the great number of they ship xxxi -- curio censure both measure say that the one be as deficient in spirit as the other exceed in it : that the latter advise a shameful flight and the former recommend we to engage at a great disadvantage for on what say he can we rely that we can storm a camp fortify both by nature and art or indeed what advantage do we gain if we give over the assault after have suffer considerable loss as if success do not acquire for a general the affection of he army and misfortune they hatred but what do a change of camp imply but a shameful flight and universal despair and the alienation of the army for neither ought the obedient to suspect that they be distrust nor the insolent to know that we fear they because we fear augment the licentiousness of the latter and diminish the zeal of the former but if say he we be convince of the truth of the report of the disaffection of the army -lrb- which i indeed be confident be either altogether groundless or at least less than they be suppose to be -rrb- how much better to conceal and hide we suspicion of it than by we conduct confirm it ought not the defect of a army to be as carefully conceal as the wound in we body lest we should increase the enemy 's hope but they moreover advise we to set out at midnight in order i suppose that those who attempt to do wrong may have a fairer opportunity for conduct of this kind be restrain either by shame or fear to the display of which the night be most adverse wherefore i be neither so rash as to give my opinion that we ought to attack they camp without hope of succeed nor so influence by fear as to despond : and i imagine that every expedient ought first to be try and i be in a great degree confident that i shall form the same opinion as yourselve on this matter xxxii -- have break up the council he call the soldier together and remind they what advantage caesar have derive from they zeal at corfinium how by they good office and influence he have bring over a great part of italy to he interest for say he all the municipal town afterwards imitate you and you conduct nor be it without reason that caesar judge so favourably and the enemy so harshly of you for pompey though beat in no engagement yet be oblige to shift he ground and leave italy from the precedent establish by you conduct caesar commit I whom he consider he dearest friend and the province of sicily and africa without which he be not able to protect rome or italy to you protection there be some here present who encourage you to revolt from we for what can they wish for more than at once to ruin we and to involve you in a heinous crime or what baser opinion could they in they resentment entertain of you than that you would betray those who acknowledge themselves indebted to you for everything and put yourselve in the power of those who think they have be ruin by you have you not hear of caesar 's exploit in spain that he route two army conquer two general recover two province and effect all this within forty day after he come in sight of the enemy can those who be not able to stand against he whilst they be uninjured resist he when they be ruin will you who take part with caesar whilst victory be uncertain take part with the conquered enemy when the fortune of the war be decide and when you ought to reap the reward of you service for they say that they have be desert and betray by you and remind you of a former oath but do you desert lucius domitius or do lucius domitius desert you do he not when you be ready to submit to the greatest difficulty cast you off do he not without you privacy endeavor to effect he own escape when you be betray by he be you not preserve by caesar 's generosity and how could he think you bind by you oath to he when after have throw up the ensign of power and abdicate he government he become a private person and a captive in another 's power a new obligation be leave upon you that you should disregard the oath by which you be at present bind and have respect only to that which be invalidate by the surrender of you general and he diminution of rank but i suppose although you be please with caesar you be offend with I however i shall not boast of my service to you which still be inferior to my own wish or you expectation but however soldier have ever look for the reward of labor at the conclusion of a war and what the issue of it be likely to be not even you can doubt but why should i omit to mention my own diligence and good fortune and to what a happy crisis affair be now arrive be you sorry that i transport the army safe and entire without the loss of a single ship that on my arrival in the very first attack i route the enemy 's fleet that twice in two day i defeat the enemy 's horse that i carry out of the very harbor and bay two hundred of the enemy 's victualler and reduce they to that situation that they can receive no supplies either by land or sea will you divorce yourselve from this fortune and these general and prefer the disgrace of corfinium the defeat of italy the surrender of both spain and the prestige of the african war i for my part make by arbitration as appoint by caesar when in rome that he would relieve they but it happen from the justice of trebonius 's decree and he humanity -lrb- for he think that in such dangerous time justice should be administer with moderation and compassion -rrb- that not one could be find who would offer himself the first to lodge a appeal for to plead poverty to complain of he own private calamity or the general distress of the time or to assert the difficulty of set the goods to sale be the behavior of a man even of a moderate temper but to retain they possession entire and at the same time acknowledge themselves in debt what sort of spirit and what impudence would it not have argue therefore nobody be find so unreasonable as to make such demand but caelius prove more severe to those very person for whose advantage it have be design and start from this beginning in order that he might not appear to have engage in so dishonourable a affair without effect something he promulgate a law that all debt should be discharge in six equal payment of six month each without interest xxi -- when servilius the consul and the other magistrate oppose he and he himself effect less than he expect in order to raise the passion of the people he drop it and promulgate two other one by which he remit the annual rent of the house to the tenant the other a act of insolvency : upon which the mob make a assault on caius trebonius and have wound several person drive he from he tribunal the consul servilius inform the senate of he proceedings who pass a decree that caelius should be remove from the management of the republic upon this decree the consul forbid he the senate and when he be attempt to harangue the people turn he out of the rostrum sting with the ignominy and with resentment he pretend in public that he would go to caesar but privately send messenger to milo who have murder clodius and have be condemn for it and have invite he into italy because he have engage the remains of the gladiator to he interest by make they supple present he join he and send he to thurinum to tamper with the shepherd when he himself be on he road to casilinum at the because the roman citizen reside there have arm themselves and think he ought to be treat as a enemy to the state he abandon he first design and change he route xxii -- milo in the meantime despatch difficulty by reason of they debt but not be able to prevail with they he set at liberty some slave from the work-house and begin to assault cosa in the district of thurinum there have receive a blow lie opposite to the harbor judge it better to guard that place which be we only pass to sea than to keep all the shore and port block up by a fleet by he sudden arrival he fall in with some of we transport and set they on fire and carry off one laden with corn he strike great terror into we man and have in the night land a party of soldier and archer he beat we guard of horse from they station and gain so much by the advantage of situation that he despatch letter to pompey that if he please he might order the rest of the ship to be haul upon shore and repair for that with he own fleet he could prevent caesar from receive he auxiliary xxiv -- antonius be at this time at brundisium and rely on the valor of he troops cover about sixty of the long-boat belong to the men-of-war with penthouse and bulwark of hurdle and put on board they select soldier and dispose they separately along the shore : and under the pretext of keep the seaman in exercise he order two three-banked galley which he have build at brundisium to row to the mouth of the port when libo see they advance boldly towards he he send five four-banked galley against they in hope of intercept they when these come near we ship we veteran soldier retreat within the harbor the enemy urge by they eagerness to capture they pursue they unguardedly for instantly the boat of antonius on a certain signal row with great violence from all part against the enemy and at the first charge take one of the four-banked galley with the seaman and marine and force the rest to flee disgracefully in addition to this loss they be prevent from get water by the horse which antonius have dispose along the sea-coast libo vex at the distress and disgrace depart from brundisium and abandon the blockade xxv -- several month have now elapse and winter be almost go and caesar 's legion and shipping be not come to he from brundisium and he imagine that some opportunity have be neglect for the wind have at least be often favourable and he think that he must trust to they at last and the longer it be defer the more eager be those who command pompey 's fleet to guard the coast and be more confident of prevent we get assistance : they receive frequent reproof from pompey by letter that as they have not prevent caesar 's arrival at the first they should at least stop the remainder of he army : and they be expect that the season for transport troops would become more unfavourable every day as the wind grow calmer caesar feeling some trouble on this account write in severe term to he officer at brundisium -lrb- and give they order -rrb- that as soon as they find the wind to answer they should not let the opportunity of set sail pass by if they be even to steer they course to the shore of apollonium : because there they might run they ship on ground that these part principally be leave unguarded by the enemy 's fleet because they dare not venture too far from the harbor xxvi -- they -lrb- he officer -rrb- exert boldness and courage aid by the instruction of marcus antonius and fufius kalenus and animated by the soldier strongly encourage they and decline no danger for caesar 's safety have get a southerly wind weigh anchor and the next day be carry past apollonium and dyrrachium and be see from the continent quintus coponius who command the rhodian fleet at dyrrachium put out of the port with he ship and when they have almost come up with we in consequence of the breeze die away the south wind spring up afresh and rescue we however he do not desist from he attempt but hope by the labor and perseverance of he seaman to be able to bear up against the violence of the storm and although we be carry beyond dyrrachium by the violence of the wind he nevertheless continue to chase we we man take advantage of fortune 's kindness for they be still afraid of be attack by the enemy 's fleet if the wind abate have come near a port call nymphaeum about three mile beyond lissus put into it -lrb- this port be protect from a south-west wind but be not secure against a south wind -rrb- and think less danger be to be apprehend from the storm than from the enemy but as soon as they be within the port the south wind which have blow for two day by extraordinary good luck veer round to the south-west xxvii -- here one might observe the sudden turn of fortune we who a moment before be alarm for ourselves be safely lodge in a very secure harbor : and they who have threaten ruin to we fleet be force to be uneasy on they own account : and thus by a change of circumstance the storm protect we ship and damage the rhodian fleet to such a degree that all they deck ship sixteen in number founder without exception and be wreck : and of the prodigious number of seaman and soldier some lose they life by be dash against the rock other be take by we man : but caesar send they all safe home xxviii -- two of we ship that have not keep up with the rest be overtake by the night and not know what port the rest have make to come to a anchor opposite lissus otacilius crassus who command pompey 's fleet detach after they several barge and small craft and attempt to take they at the same time he treat with they about capitulate and promise they they life if they would surrender one of they carry two hundred and twenty recruit the other be man with somewhat less than two hundred veteran here it might be see what security man derive from a resolute spirit for the recruit frighten at the number of vessel and fatigue with the rolling of the sea and with sea-sickness surrender to otacilius after have first receive he oath that the enemy would not injure they but as soon as they be bring before he contrary to the obligation of he oath they be inhumanly put to death in he presence but the soldier of the veteran legion who have also struggle not only with the inclemency of the weather but by labor at the pump think it they duty to remit nothing of they former valor : and have protracted the beginning of the night in settle the term under pretence of surrender they oblige the pilot to run the ship aground : and have get a convenient place on the shore they spend have before assign they and have carefully fortify receive antony into they town and give he every assistance otacilius apprehensive for he own safety escape out of the town and go to pompey all he the ponton which be a sort of gallic ship he leave at lissus with this object that if pompey imagine italy defenceless should transport he army thither -lrb- and this notion be spread among the common convenient situation xxxi -- during these time scipio though he have sustain some loss near mount amanus have assume to himself the title of imperator after which he demand large sum of money from the state and prince he have also exact from the tax-gatherer two year ' rent that they owe and enjoin they to lend he the amount of the next year and demand a supply of horse from the whole province when they be collect leave behind he he neighbouring enemy the parthian -lrb- who shortly before have kill marcus crassus the imperator and have keep marcus bibulus besiege -rrb- he draw he legion and cavalry out of syrium and when he come into the province which be under great anxiety and fear of the parthian war and hear some declaration of the soldier that they would march against a enemy if he attach they more firmly to he interest permit they to plunder the city xxxii -- in the meantime the money which have be demand from the province at large be most rigorously exact besides many new impost of different kind be devise to gratify he avarice a tax of so much a head be lay on every slave and child column door corn soldier sailor arm engine and carriage be make subject to a duty wherever a name could be find for anything it be deem a sufficient reason for levy money on it officer be appoint to collect it not only in the city but in almost every village and fort : and whosoever of they act with the greatest rigor and inhumanity be esteem the best man and best citizen the province be overrun with bailiff and officer and crowd with overseer and tax-gatherer who besides the duty impose exact a gratuity for themselves for they assert that be expel from they own home and country they stand in need of every necessary endeavoring by a plausible pretence to color the most infamous conduct to this be add the most exorbitant interest as usually happen in time of war the whole sum be call in on which occasion they allege that the delay of a single day be a donation therefore in those two year the debt of the province be double : but notwithstanding tax be exact not only from the roman citizen but from every corporation and every state and they say that these be loan exact by the senate 's decree the tax of the ensue year be demand beforehand as a loan from the collector as on they first appointment xxxiii -- moreover scipio order the money formerly lodge in the temple of diana at ephesus to be take out with the statue of that goddess which remain there when scipio come to the temple letter be deliver to he from pompey in the presence of several he receive the letter he dismiss he attendant and begin to prepare for he journey to macedonium and a few day after set out this circumstance save the money at ephesus xxxiv -- caesar have effect a xxxv -- of these calvisius on he first arrival in aetolium be very kindly receive dislodge the enemy 's garrison in calydon and naupactus and make himself master of the whole country cassius go to thessaly with he legion as there be two faction there he find the citizen divide in they inclination hegasaretus a man of established power favor pompey 's interest petreius a young man of a most cassius and the expedition of scipio favonius xxxvii -- scipio have stay for two day in he camp along the river haliacmon which run between he and domitius 's camp on the third day at dawn lead he to engage suspect that he should be oblige the next day either to fight against he inclination or to incur great disgrace by keep within he camp though he have come with high expectation yet by advance rashly make a shameful end and at night cross the river without even give the signal for break up the camp and return to the ground from which he come and there encamp near the river on a come there as usual they suddenly rush from they ambush but we man bravely support they charge and return quickly every man to he own rank and in they turn make a general charge on the enemy : and have kill about eighty of they and put the rest to flight retreat to they camp with the loss of only two man xxxviii -- after these transaction domitius hope to allure scipio to a battle pretend to be oblige to change he position through want of corn and have give the signal for decamp advanced about three mile and post he army and cavalry in a convenient place conceal from the enemy 's view scipio be in readiness to pursue he detach he cavalry and a considerable number of light infantry to explore domitius 's route when they have march a short way and they foremost troops be within reach of we discover they plot and think it in vain to wait for any more have get two troops in they power intercept they among they be marcus opimius general of the horse but he make he escape : they either kill or take prisoner all the rest of these two troops and bring they to domitius xxxix -- caesar have draw he garrison out of the sea-port as before mention leave three cohort at oricum to protect the and face it to the entrance of the port and fill it with soldier and order they to keep guard against any sudden attack xl -- cneius pompey 's son who command the egyptian fleet have get intelligence of these thing come to oricum and weigh up the ship that have be sink with a windlass and by strain at it with several rope and attack the other which have be place by acilius to watch the port with several ship on which he have raise very high turret so that fight as it be from a eminence and send fresh man constantly to relieve the fatigued and at the same time attempt the town on all side by and set the rest on fire after despatch this business he leave decimus laelius whom he have take away from the command of the asiatic fleet to hinder provision from be bring into the town from bibli and amantium and go himself to lissus where he attack thirty merchantman leave within the port by antonius and set they on fire he attempt to storm lissus but be delay three day by the vigorous -- as soon as caesar hear that pompey be at asparagium he set out for that place with he army and have take the capital of the parthinian on he march where there be a garrison of pompey 's he reach pompey in macedonium on the third day and encamp beside he and the day follow have draw out all he force before he camp he offer pompey battle but perceive that he keep within he trench he lead he army back to he camp and thought of pursue some other plan accordingly the day follow he set out with all he force by a long circuit through a difficult and narrow road to dyrrachium hope either that pompey would be compel to follow he to dyrrachium or that he communication with it might be cut off because he have deposit there all he provision and mat -lrb- ` e -rrb- riel of war and so it happen for pompey at first not know he design because he imagine he have take a route in a different direction from that country think that the scarcity of provision have oblige he to shift he quarter but from dyrrachium as he be unable to effect he purpose take a new resolution and entrenched himself strongly on a rise ground which be call petra where ship of a small size can come in and be sheltered from some wind here he order a part of he men-of-war to attend he and corn and provision to be bring from asia and from all the country of which he keep possession caesar imagine that the war would be protracted to too great a length and despairing of he convoy from italy because all the coast be guard with great diligence by pompey 's adherent and because he own fleet which he have build during the winter in sicily gaul and italy be detain send lucius canuleius into epirus to procure corn and because these country be too remote he fix granary in certain place and regulate the carriage of the corn for the neighbouring state he likewise give direction that search should be make for whatever corn be in lissus the country of the parthinus and all the place of strength the quantity be very small both from the nature of the land -lrb- for the country be rough and mountainous and the people commonly import what grain they use -rrb- and because pompey have foresee what would happen and some day before have plunder the parthinus and have ravage and dig up they house carry off all the corn which he collect by means of he horse xliii -- caesar on be inform of these transaction pursue measure suggest by the nature of the country for round pompey 's camp there be several high and rough hill these he first of all occupy with guard and raise strong fort on they then draw a fortification from one fort to another as the nature of each position allow he begin to draw a line of circumvallation round pompey with these view as he have but a small quantity of corn and pompey be strong in cavalry that he might furnish he army with corn and other necessaries from all side with less danger : secondly to prevent pompey from forage and thereby render he horse ineffectual in the operation of the war and thirdly to lessen he reputation on which he see he depend greatly among foreign nation when a report should have spread throughout the world that he be blockade by caesar and dare not hazard a battle xliv -- neither be pompey willing to leave the sea and dyrrachium because he have lodge he mat -lrb- ` e -rrb- riel there he weapon arm and engine and supply he army with corn from it by he ship : nor be he able to put a stop to caesar 's work without hazard a battle which at that time he have determine not to do nothing be leave but to adopt the last resource namely to possess himself of as many hill as he could and cover as great a extent of country as possible with he troops and divide caesar 's force as much as possible and so it happen : for have raise twenty-four fort and take in a compass of fifteen mile he get forage in this space and within this circuit there be several field lately sow in which the cattle might feed in the meantime and as we man who have complete they work by draw line of communication from one fort to another be afraid that pompey 's man would sally out from some part and attack we in the rear so the enemy be make a continued fortification in a circuit within ours to prevent we from break in on any side or surround they on the rear but they complete they work first both because they have a greater number of man and because they have a smaller compass to enclose when caesar attempt to gain any place though pompey have resolve not to oppose he with he whole force or to come to a general engagement yet he detach to particular place slinger and archer with which he army abound and several of we man be wound and fill with great dread of the arrow and almost all the soldier make coat or covering for themselves of hair cloth tarpaulin or raw hide to defend they against the weapon xlv -- in seize the post each exert he utmost power : caesar to confine pompey within as narrow a compass as possible pompey to occupy as many hill as he could in as large a circuit as possible and several skirmish be fight in consequence of it in one of these when caesar 's ninth legion have gain a certain post and have begin to fortify it pompey possess himself of a hill near to and opposite the same place and endeavor to annoy the man while at work and as the approach on one side be almost level he first surround it with archer and slinger and afterwards by detach a strong party of light infantry and use he engine he stop we work : and it be no easy matter for we man at once to defend themselves and to proceed with they fortification when caesar perceive that he troops be wound from all side he determine to retreat and give up the post he retreat be down a precipice on which account they push on with more spirit and would not allow we to retire because they imagine that we resign the place through fear it be report that pompey say that day in triumph to he friend about he that he would consent to be account a general of no experience if caesar 's legion effect a retreat without considerable loss from that ground into which they have rashly advanced xlvi -- caesar be uneasy about the retreat of he soldier order hurdle to be carry to the further side of the hill and to be place opposite to the enemy and behind they a trench of a moderate breadth to be sink by he soldier under shelter of the hurdle : and the ground to be make as difficult as possible he himself disposed slinger in convenient place to cover we man in they retreat these thing be complete he order he legion to file off pompey 's man insultingly and boldly pursued and chase we level the hurdle that be throw up in the front of we work in order to pass over the trench which as soon as caesar perceive be afraid that he man would appear not to retreat but to be repulse and that greater loss might be sustain when he man be almost half way down the hill he encourage they by antonius who command that legion order the signal of battle to be sound and a charge to be make on the enemy the soldier of the ninth legion suddenly close they file throw they javelin and advance impetuously from the low ground up the steep drive pompey 's man precipitately before they and oblige they to turn they back but they retreat be greatly impede by the hurdle that lay in a long line before they and the pallisado which be in they way and the trench that be sink but we man be contented to retreat without injury have kill several of the enemy and lose but five of they own very quietly retire and have seize some other hill somewhat on this side of that place complete they fortification xlvii -- this method of conduct a war be new and unusual as well on account of the number of fort the extent and greatness of the work and the manner of attack and defense as on account of other circumstance for all who have attempt to besiege any person have attack the enemy when they be frightened or weak or after a defeat or have be keep in fear of some attack when they themselves have have a superior force both of foot and horse besides the usual design of a siege be to cut off the enemy 's supplies on the contrary caesar with a inferior force be enclose troops sound and unhurt and who have abundance of all thing for there arrive every day a prodigious number of ship which bring they provision : nor could the wind blow from any point that would not be favourable to some of they whereas caesar have consume all the corn far and near be in very great distress but he soldier bear all with uncommon patience for they remember that they lay under the same difficulty last year in spain and yet by labor and patience have conclude a dangerous war they recollect too that they have suffer a alarming scarcity at alesium and a much greater at avaricum and yet have return victorious over mighty nation they refuse neither barley nor pulse when offer they and they hold in great esteem cattle of which they get great quantity from epirus xlviii -- there be a sort of root call chara discover by the troops which serve under valerius this they mix up with milk and it greatly contribute to relieve they want they make it into a sort of bread they have great plenty of it : loaf make of this when pompey 's man upbraid ours with want they frequently throw among they to damp they hope xlix -- the corn be now begin to ripen and they hope support they want as they be confident of have abundance in a short time and there be frequently hear declaration of the soldier on guard in discourse with each other that they would rather live on the bark of the tree than let pompey escape from they hand for they be often tell by deserter that they could scarcely maintain they horse and that they other cattle be dead : -rrb- that he might not be think to have assume the part of the general one circumstance lay the pompeian under great difficulty in make good a retreat : for they have advance from disadvantageous it ever in expectation as may be conjecture that caesar would expose himself to this disadvantageous situation caesar see no likelihood of be able to bring pompey to a action judge it the most the signal for march be give and the tent strike it be observe that shortly before contrary to he daily practice pompey 's army have advance farther than usual from he entrenchment so that it appear for the force be divide and the fight maintain in several street at once and the enemy endeavor to seize with a strong party the ship of war of which fifty have be send to pompey 's assistance but after the battle in thessaly have return home they be all of either three or five bank of oar well equip and appoint with every necessary for a voyage besides these there be twenty-two vessel with deck which be usually keep at alexandrium to guard the port if they make themselves master of these caesar be deprive of he fleet they would have the command of the port and whole sea and could prevent he from procure provision and auxiliary accordingly that spirit be display which ought to be display when the one party see that a speedy victory depend on the issue and the other they safety but caesar gain the day and set fire to all those ship and to other which be in the dock because he could not guard so many place with so small a force and immediately he convey some troops to the pharo by he ship cxil -- the pharo be a tower on a island of prodigious height build with amazing work and take its name from the island this island lie over against alexandria form a harbor but on the upper side it be connect with the town by a narrow way eight hundred pace in length make by pile sink in the sea and by a bridge in this island some of the egyptian have house and a village as large as a town and whatever ship from any quarter either through mistake the channel or by the storm have be drive from they course upon the coast they constantly plunder like pirate and without the consent of those who be master of the pharo no vessel can enter the harbor on account of its narrowness caesar be greatly alarm on this account whilst the enemy be engage in battle land he soldier seize the pharo and place a garrison in it by this mean he gain this point that he could be supply without danger with corn and auxiliary : for he send to all the neighbouring country to demand supplies in other part of the town they fight so obstinately that they quit the field with equal advantage and neither be beat -lrb- in consequence of the narrowness of the pass -rrb- and a few be kill on both side caesar secure the most necessary post and fortify they in the night in this quarter of the town be a wing of the king 's palace in which caesar be lodge on he first arrival and a theater adjoining the house which serve as for citadel and command a avenue to the port and other dock these fortification he increase during the succeed day that he might have they before he as a rampart and not be oblige to fight against he will in the meantime ptolemy 's younger daughter hope the throne would become vacant make she escape from the palace to achilla and assist he in prosecute the war but they soon quarrel about the command which circumstance enlarged the present to the soldier for each endeavor by great sacrifice to secure they affection whilst the enemy be thus employ pothinus tutor to the young king and regent of the kingdom who be in caesar 's part of the town send messenger to achilla and encourage he not to desist from he enterprise nor to despair of success but he messenger be discover and apprehend he be put to death by caesar such be the commencement of the alexandrian war \* \* \* \* \* index nb the numeral refer to the book the figure to the chapter formerly divide from gaul it spring out of the rhaetian alp in the western border of switzerland and the northern of the grison from two spring which unite near coire and fall into the meuse and the german ocean by two mouth whence virgil call it rhenus bicorni it pass through lacus brigantinus or the lake of constance and lacus acronius or the lake of zell and then continue its westerly direction to basle -lrb- basilia -rrb- it then bend northward and separate germany from france and further down germany from belgium at schenk the rhine send off its left-hand branch the vahali -lrb- waal -rrb- by a western course to join the mosa or meuse the rhine then flow on a few mile and again separate into two branch -- the one to the right call the flevo or felvus or flevum -- now the yssel and the other call the helium now the _ leek _ the latter join the mosa above rotterdam the yssel be first connect with the rhine by the canal of drusus it pass through the small lake of flevo before reach the sea which become expand into what be now call the zuyder zee by increase of water through the yssel from the rhine the whole course of the rhine be nine hundred mile of which six
